Also, by intending supererogatory or another obligatory [fast], it is only for Ramadan. And what is meant by this error: opposite of correctness, not opposite of intentional; for the intentional and the mistaken are equal in this ruling. Except the traveler who intends another obligatory [fast] according to Abu Hanifa. An exception from an implicit [phrase] meaning he hits Ramadan with an error in description for everyone except the traveler when he intends in Ramadan another obligatory [fast] of make-up or vow, then it falls for what he intended, not for Ramadan according to Abu Hanifa; because when the obligation of performing fell in his case, he thereafter chooses between eating and another obligatory [fast]. But according to both [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], it is not valid because the witnessing of the month exists in his case like the resident; he was merely granted the concession to break fast for ease, so if he does not take the concession, his ruling returns to the original, so it does not fall for what he intended but for Ramadan. And this traveler is engaged. And what is meant by this is to repel a misunderstanding that the apparent from 'error' in the author's statement that if he intended supererogatory or another obligatory in Ramadan intentionally, it would be for Ramadan—its repelling is apparent. (al-Sanbali) Opposite of correctness; so correctness in Ramadan is to fast for Ramadan, not for other than it; if he intends other than it, supererogatory or another obligatory, he has erred whether this intention was intentional or mistaken. (al-Qamar) 'Exception etc.' repels an apparent difficulty: that it is an exception from 'he hits the absolute name,' and it is invalid from several aspects: first, the excepted is not of the same genus as the excepted-from; second, the excepted-from is not multiple; both are necessary in the continuous exception which is the original; third, it necessitates that the traveler does not hit the absolute name, contrary to reality, for if he intends the absolute fast it suffices for the obligation. So he answered as you see, and its summary is that the exception is attached to his statement: 'the error in description,' not to 'the absolute name.' (al-Sanbali) 'While he is' etc. indicates that his statement 'intends' etc. is a circumstantial qualifier of 'traveler,' and in it the circumstantial qualifier from the object of the preposition is not known; except it be said that it is a circumstantial qualifier of the pronoun in 'traveler' because the meaning is 'except the one who traveled,' so the definite article is relative. (al-Qamar) 'And according to both etc.' explains the benefit of the restriction in the text with his statement 'according to Abu Hanifa.' (al-Qamar) 'And according to both etc.' They both say: The legislation of fasting is general for both resident and traveler because its obligation is due to witnessing the month, and that has been realized in his case as in the resident's, so if he fasts for the time's obligation it suffices, so nothing remains besides the time's fast as legislated for the traveler as well. And Abu Hanifa has two ways in answering their statement; if you wish to be informed of them, consult 'al-Tahqiq' Sharh al-Hisami. (al-Sanbali) 'For ease': This concession for ease does not permit that other than Ramadan fast be made legislated in it, so when he does not take the concession etc. (al-Qamar) 'And this traveler is engaged': He only added this to indicate that the author's statement 'unlike the sick person' is an adverbial phrase. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn concerning the ruling of intending a different fast in Ramadan. The author first states a general rule: if someone intends a supererogatory or another obligatory fast in Ramadan, it counts only for Ramadan, whether the intention was intentional or mistaken. However, an exception is made for the traveler. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a traveler—who is permitted to break his fast—intends a different obligatory fast (like a make-up or vow), his fast counts for what he intended, not for Ramadan. This is because the obligation to perform Ramadan fasting has been lifted from him due to his travel, giving him a real choice between eating and another fast. Therefore, his intention is effective. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree. They argue that the obligation of Ramadan remains incumbent because the traveler witnesses the month just like the resident. The permission to break is merely a concession for ease; if the traveler chooses not to take that concession and fasts, his fast defaults to the Ramadan obligation. Thus, his intention for another fast is invalid and it reverts to Ramadan. The commentator then addresses various linguistic and usul points, such as why the word 'error' is used and how the exception is properly structured. He also notes that the restriction 'according to Abu Hanifa' in the matn indicates that the Sahibayn differ. The passage emphasizes the Hanafi position that the traveler's concession grants a genuine choice, not merely a dispensation.

Key Terms
الخطأ (al-khata’): Error in intention: intending a fast other than Ramadan during Ramadan, whether intentional or mistaken.
المسافر (al-musafir): A traveler who embarks on a journey that permits breaking the Ramadan fast.
استثناء (istithna’): An exception from the general rule that intending another fast in Ramadan counts for Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a traveler intends a different obligatory fast (e.g., a make-up fast) during Ramadan according to Abu Hanifa?
A) It counts for the Ramadan obligation.
B) It counts for what he intended (the make-up fast).
C) It is invalid and he must fast another day.
D) It counts for Ramadan only if he traveled before fajr.

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn hinges on whether a traveler's concession removes the obligation of performing Ramadan or merely permits its omission while the obligation remains.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Sick Person's Intent for Another Fast: The Hanafi Rule
Contrasts the sick person's ruling with the traveler's and records two narrations for the traveler's supererogatory fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that if a sick person with a concession to break fast fasts and intends another fast, his fast counts for Ramadan, and apply the distinction between actual and potential inability.

Core Idea
If a sick person fasts despite a concession, his fast counts for Ramadan, not a different intention.

This lesson examines a key usul principle regarding concessions (rukhas). In the Hanafi school, the sick person's permission to break fast is tied to actual inability, not mere choice. If he fasts, it proves ability, so the fast satisfies the Ramadan obligation. This contrasts with the traveler, whose concession is for ease. We will explore the rule, the minority view, and a reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of inability
Distinguish actual inability (al-'ajz al-haqiqi) from potential inability (al-'ajz al-taqdiri). The sick person's concession is tied to the first.
Actual inability means he cannot fast without severe harm.
2
Apply the rule: fasting shows ability
If he fasts voluntarily, it demonstrates he was actually able, so his fast must be applied to the default obligation (Ramadan), not his intended make-up or supererogatory.
3
Contrast with the traveler
The traveler's concession is not about inability but about choice. Therefore, if a traveler intends another fast, it can count for that intention.
This distinction is crucial.
4
Examine the minority view and reconciliation
Some say the sick person's concession is also potential, making him like the traveler. A reconciliation distinguishes types of illness.
This is an ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف المريض، فإنه إن نوى نفلاً أو واجبًا آخر لم يقع عما نوى؛ لأن رخصته متعلقة بحقيقة العجز لا العجز التقديري، فإذا صام وتحمل المحنة على نفسه عُلمَ أنه لم يكن عاجزاً، فيقع عن رمضان، وهذا هو المختار، وقيل رخصته أيضًا متعلقة بالعجز التقديري، وهو خوف زيادة المرض فهو كالمسافر، وقيل في التطبيق بينهما: إن المريض الذي يضر به الصوم كمرض حمى البرد، ووجع العين، فرخصته متعلقة بخوف ازدياد المرض، والعجز التقديري، والمريض الذي لا يضر به الصوم كمرض امتلاء البطن، فرخصته متعلقة بحقيقة العجز، فإذا صام هذا المريض ظهر أنه لم يكن له عجز حقيقي، فلا يقع عما نوى بل عن رمضان. وفي النفل عنه روايتان متعلق بقوله: ينوي واجبًا آخر أي في صوم النفل للمسافر عن أبي حنيفة له روايتان في رواية الحسن يقع عما نوى وفي رواية ابن سماعة عن رمضان. أي الحسن بن زياد وهو ظاهر الرواية لم يقع عما نوى بل عن رمضان وهو الصحيح كذا في الأشباه. (القمر) لا العجز التقديري: أي الفرضي الاحتمالي بأن خاف زيادة المرض. (القمر) وقيل: القائل صاحب التوضيح. (القمر) بالعجز التقديري لا بالعجز التحقيقي وهو أن لا يقدر على الصوم. (القمر) فهو كالمسافر: فيقع الصوم عما نوى واختاره أكثر المشايخ كذا قال ابن الملك لله. (القمر) وقيل في التطبيق بينهما أي بين الروايتين، والقائل هو الشيخ عبد العزيز كذا قال العلي القاري، وقال بحر العلوم ولي في هذه المحاكمة نظر؛ لأن النوع الذي لا يضر معه الصوم لا يرخص فيه المريض أصلا فهو خارج من موضوع البحث إلا إذا بلغ إلى الضعف الذي يضر معه الصوم، فحينئذ يرخص؛ لئلا يزداد الضعف فاندرج هذا في النوع الأول، ثم اعلم أن بعض الشراح قدحوا في هذا التطبيق بأنه مما يعرفه المدقق في علم الطب لا كان متوكلاً على الله شاغلاً بطاعته، وأنت تعلم ما فيه، فإن إباحة التيمم متعلقة بخوف ازدياد المرض مع أنه لا ينافي التوكل والاشتغال بالطاعة كذا في الصبح الصادق. (القمر) من فرخصته متعلقة إلخ: فهو كالمسافر، فنية الواجب الآخر تصح عنه. (القمر) عما نوى وهو اختيار شيخ الإسلام صاحب الهداية والقاضي فخر الدين والشيخ الكبير أبي الفضل لله. (المحشي) وفي رواية ابن سماعة إلخ وهو الأصح كذا في التلويح وقال العلي القاري وإنما قيل: الأصح؛ احترازًا عما قيل: إنه يقع عن الفرض على رواية ابن سماعة، وعن النفل على مقتضى رواية الحسن. (القمر)
Unlike the sick person, for if he intends a supererogatory or another obligatory [fast], it does not fall for what he intended because his concession is linked to actual inability, not to potential inability. So if he fasts and bears the hardship upon himself, it is known that he was not unable, so it falls for Ramadan. This is the chosen view. And it was said that his concession is also linked to potential inability, i.e., fear of increase of illness, so he is like the traveler. And there is a word on reconciling between them: that the sick person for whom fasting is harmful, like the illness of cold fever and eye pain, his concession is linked to fear of increase of illness and potential inability; and the sick person for whom fasting is not harmful, like the illness of stomach fullness, his concession is linked to actual inability. So if this sick person fasts, it appears that he had no actual inability, so it does not fall for what he intended but for Ramadan. And regarding the supererogatory [fast] from him, there are two narrations attached to his statement: 'intends another obligatory' meaning concerning the supererogatory fast of the traveler from Abu Hanifa. He has two narrations: in the narration of al-Hasan, it falls for what he intended; and in the narration of Ibn Sam'ah, it falls for Ramadan. That is al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and this is the apparent narration: it does not fall for what he intended but for Ramadan, and it is the correct one. Thus in al-Ashbah. (al-Qamar) 'Not potential inability': i.e., hypothetical/possible inability by fearing increase of illness. (al-Qamar) 'And it was said': the speaker is the author of al-Tawdih. (al-Qamar) 'By potential inability' not by actual inability, which is being unable to fast. (al-Qamar) 'So he is like the traveler': so the fast falls for what he intended, and this was chosen by most shuyukh as said by Ibn al-Malik. (al-Qamar) 'And there is a word on reconciling between them' i.e., between the two narrations; the speaker is Shaykh Abd al-Aziz, as said by Ali al-Qari. And Bahr al-Ulum said: I have reservations about this comparison, because the type where fasting is not harmful is not permitted for the sick person at all; it is outside the subject matter of discussion unless it reaches a weakness where fasting is harmful; then it is permitted; so that it does not increase weakness, so this falls under the first type. Then know that some commentators criticized this reconciliation as something that a specialist in medicine would know, not one relying on Allah and occupied with His obedience. And you know what is in it, for the permission of tayammum is linked to fear of increase of illness, and it does not contradict reliance and occupation with obedience. Thus in al-Subh al-Sadiq. (al-Qamar) 'From his concession is linked etc.': so he is like the traveler; the intention of another obligatory is valid from him. (al-Qamar) 'From what he intended' and this is the choice of Shaykh al-Islam, author of al-Hidaya, and Qadi Fakhr al-Din, and the great shaykh Abu al-Fadl. (al-Muhashi) 'And in the narration of Ibn Sam'ah etc.' and it is the most correct, thus in al-Talwih. And Ali al-Qari said: it was only called the most correct as a protection from what was said: that it falls for the obligation according to Ibn Sam'ah's narration, and for the supererogatory according to the purport of al-Hasan's narration. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage contrasts the sick person with the traveler. The sick person's concession (permission to break fast) is based on actual inability—if he truly cannot fast, he may break; but if he chooses to fast, it shows he is able, so his fast counts for Ramadan. If he intends another fast, it does not count for that intention. The traveler's concession is based on a choice for ease, not inability. There is a minority view that the sick person's concession is also potential (fearing increased illness), making him like the traveler. A reconciliation distinguishes two types of sickness: one where fasting is actually harmful (e.g., fever), linked to potential inability; another where it is not harmful (e.g., stomach fullness), linked to actual inability. The commentator notes criticisms of this medical distinction, citing tayammum as a parallel. The passage also records two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the traveler's supererogatory fast: one (from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) says it falls for the supererogatory intention; the other (from Ibn Sam'ah) says it falls for Ramadan. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it falls for Ramadan, which is also the choice of major later scholars. The 'most correct' designation guards against confusing the two narrations.

Key Terms
العجز الحقيقي (al-'ajz al-haqiqi): Actual inability to fast without severe harm or hardship.
العجز التقديري (al-'ajz al-taqdiri): Potential inability: fearing increase of illness if one fasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His intended fast
B) Ramadan
C) It is invalid
D) It depends

Key Takeaway
The sick person's fast always satisfies the Ramadan obligation when he fasts voluntarily, overriding any other intention.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

The Traveler's Supererogatory Fast: Two Narrations and the Relied-Upon View
Contrasts the sick person's ruling with the traveler's and records two narrations for the traveler's supererogatory fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the traveler's nafal fast, state which is Zahir al-Riwayah, and explain why the relied-upon view is that it counts for Ramadan.

Core Idea
The traveler's supererogatory fast counts for Ramadan, not for the nafal intended—despite a minority narration.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on the traveler's supererogatory fast. Abu Hanifa has two narrations: one from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (falls for nafal) and one from Ibn Sam'ah (falls for Ramadan). The latter is the basis of the fatwa. We will analyze the tarjih and understand why the 'most correct' designation guards against confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
From Abu Hanifa: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reports it falls for the intended nafal; Ibn Sam'ah reports it falls for Ramadan.
Both are valid transmissions from the imam.
2
Determine which is Zahir al-Riwayah
Zahir al-Riwayah is the narration of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, which is well-known and transmitted through Imam Muhammad's core books.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the standard authority, but not always the mufta bihi.
3
Understand the tarjih
Despite Zahir al-Riwayah, the majority of later scholars (Shaykh al-Islam, Qadi Fakhr al-Din, etc.) adopted Ibn Sam'ah's narration, making it the mufta bihi.
The tarjih is based on later ijma' and strength of evidence.
4
Note the reason for 'asahh'
The passage calls Ibn Sam'ah's narration 'the most correct' to prevent confusion between the two, clarifying that it is the operative view.
'Asahh' means more correct, indicating preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف المريض، فإنه إن نوى نفلاً أو واجبًا آخر لم يقع عما نوى؛ لأن رخصته متعلقة بحقيقة العجز لا العجز التقديري، فإذا صام وتحمل المحنة على نفسه عُلمَ أنه لم يكن عاجزاً، فيقع عن رمضان، وهذا هو المختار، وقيل رخصته أيضًا متعلقة بالعجز التقديري، وهو خوف زيادة المرض فهو كالمسافر، وقيل في التطبيق بينهما: إن المريض الذي يضر به الصوم كمرض حمى البرد، ووجع العين، فرخصته متعلقة بخوف ازدياد المرض، والعجز التقديري، والمريض الذي لا يضر به الصوم كمرض امتلاء البطن، فرخصته متعلقة بحقيقة العجز، فإذا صام هذا المريض ظهر أنه لم يكن له عجز حقيقي، فلا يقع عما نوى بل عن رمضان. وفي النفل عنه روايتان متعلق بقوله: ينوي واجبًا آخر أي في صوم النفل للمسافر عن أبي حنيفة له روايتان في رواية الحسن يقع عما نوى وفي رواية ابن سماعة عن رمضان. أي الحسن بن زياد وهو ظاهر الرواية لم يقع عما نوى بل عن رمضان وهو الصحيح كذا في الأشباه. (القمر) لا العجز التقديري: أي الفرضي الاحتمالي بأن خاف زيادة المرض. (القمر) وقيل: القائل صاحب التوضيح. (القمر) بالعجز التقديري لا بالعجز التحقيقي وهو أن لا يقدر على الصوم. (القمر) فهو كالمسافر: فيقع الصوم عما نوى واختاره أكثر المشايخ كذا قال ابن الملك لله. (القمر) وقيل في التطبيق بينهما أي بين الروايتين، والقائل هو الشيخ عبد العزيز كذا قال العلي القاري، وقال بحر العلوم ولي في هذه المحاكمة نظر؛ لأن النوع الذي لا يضر معه الصوم لا يرخص فيه المريض أصلا فهو خارج من موضوع البحث إلا إذا بلغ إلى الضعف الذي يضر معه الصوم، فحينئذ يرخص؛ لئلا يزداد الضعف فاندرج هذا في النوع الأول، ثم اعلم أن بعض الشراح قدحوا في هذا التطبيق بأنه مما يعرفه المدقق في علم الطب لا كان متوكلاً على الله شاغلاً بطاعته، وأنت تعلم ما فيه، فإن إباحة التيمم متعلقة بخوف ازدياد المرض مع أنه لا ينافي التوكل والاشتغال بالطاعة كذا في الصبح الصادق. (القمر) من فرخصته متعلقة إلخ: فهو كالمسافر، فنية الواجب الآخر تصح عنه. (القمر) عما نوى وهو اختيار شيخ الإسلام صاحب الهداية والقاضي فخر الدين والشيخ الكبير أبي الفضل لله. (المحشي) وفي رواية ابن سماعة إلخ وهو الأصح كذا في التلويح وقال العلي القاري وإنما قيل: الأصح؛ احترازًا عما قيل: إنه يقع عن الفرض على رواية ابن سماعة، وعن النفل على مقتضى رواية الحسن. (القمر)
Unlike the sick person, for if he intends a supererogatory or another obligatory [fast], it does not fall for what he intended because his concession is linked to actual inability, not to potential inability. So if he fasts and bears the hardship upon himself, it is known that he was not unable, so it falls for Ramadan. This is the chosen view. And it was said that his concession is also linked to potential inability, i.e., fear of increase of illness, so he is like the traveler. And there is a word on reconciling between them: that the sick person for whom fasting is harmful, like the illness of cold fever and eye pain, his concession is linked to fear of increase of illness and potential inability; and the sick person for whom fasting is not harmful, like the illness of stomach fullness, his concession is linked to actual inability. So if this sick person fasts, it appears that he had no actual inability, so it does not fall for what he intended but for Ramadan. And regarding the supererogatory [fast] from him, there are two narrations attached to his statement: 'intends another obligatory' meaning concerning the supererogatory fast of the traveler from Abu Hanifa. He has two narrations: in the narration of al-Hasan, it falls for what he intended; and in the narration of Ibn Sam'ah, it falls for Ramadan. That is al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and this is the apparent narration: it does not fall for what he intended but for Ramadan, and it is the correct one. Thus in al-Ashbah. (al-Qamar) 'Not potential inability': i.e., hypothetical/possible inability by fearing increase of illness. (al-Qamar) 'And it was said': the speaker is the author of al-Tawdih. (al-Qamar) 'By potential inability' not by actual inability, which is being unable to fast. (al-Qamar) 'So he is like the traveler': so the fast falls for what he intended, and this was chosen by most shuyukh as said by Ibn al-Malik. (al-Qamar) 'And there is a word on reconciling between them' i.e., between the two narrations; the speaker is Shaykh Abd al-Aziz, as said by Ali al-Qari. And Bahr al-Ulum said: I have reservations about this comparison, because the type where fasting is not harmful is not permitted for the sick person at all; it is outside the subject matter of discussion unless it reaches a weakness where fasting is harmful; then it is permitted; so that it does not increase weakness, so this falls under the first type. Then know that some commentators criticized this reconciliation as something that a specialist in medicine would know, not one relying on Allah and occupied with His obedience. And you know what is in it, for the permission of tayammum is linked to fear of increase of illness, and it does not contradict reliance and occupation with obedience. Thus in al-Subh al-Sadiq. (al-Qamar) 'From his concession is linked etc.': so he is like the traveler; the intention of another obligatory is valid from him. (al-Qamar) 'From what he intended' and this is the choice of Shaykh al-Islam, author of al-Hidaya, and Qadi Fakhr al-Din, and the great shaykh Abu al-Fadl. (al-Muhashi) 'And in the narration of Ibn Sam'ah etc.' and it is the most correct, thus in al-Talwih. And Ali al-Qari said: it was only called the most correct as a protection from what was said: that it falls for the obligation according to Ibn Sam'ah's narration, and for the supererogatory according to the purport of al-Hasan's narration. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage contrasts the sick person with the traveler. The sick person's concession (permission to break fast) is based on actual inability—if he truly cannot fast, he may break; but if he chooses to fast, it shows he is able, so his fast counts for Ramadan. If he intends another fast, it does not count for that intention. The traveler's concession is based on a choice for ease, not inability. There is a minority view that the sick person's concession is also potential (fearing increased illness), making him like the traveler. A reconciliation distinguishes two types of sickness: one where fasting is actually harmful (e.g., fever), linked to potential inability; another where it is not harmful (e.g., stomach fullness), linked to actual inability. The commentator notes criticisms of this medical distinction, citing tayammum as a parallel. The passage also records two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the traveler's supererogatory fast: one (from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) says it falls for the supererogatory intention; the other (from Ibn Sam'ah) says it falls for Ramadan. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it falls for Ramadan, which is also the choice of major later scholars. The 'most correct' designation guards against confusing the two narrations.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/well-known narration from Abu Hanifa (specific to the traveler's supererogatory fast).
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct; a stronger narration or view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which narration is described as 'Zahir al-Riwayah' for the traveler's supererogatory fast?
A) Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration
B) Ibn Sam'ah's narration
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the traveler's nafal fast in Ramadan counts for Ramadan, based on the narration of Ibn Sam'ah.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Concept of al-Waqt al-Mushkil in Hanafi Usul
Defines the fourth type of time with the Hajj example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-waqt al-mushkil and distinguish its two aspects (container and measure) using the example of Hajj.

Core Idea
A time that is both a container (surplus) and a measure (single act) is called 'problematic' – Hajj is its only instance.

In Hanafi usul, the time for an obligation can be classified into four types: container (zarf), measure (mi'yar), shared (mushtarak), and problematic (mushkil). This lesson explores the last type, where the time simultaneously has surplus beyond the act (like a container) yet can only accommodate one performance of that act (like a measure). The classic example is the time for Hajj, which spans months but only allows one Hajj in a lifetime. Understanding this classification is essential for deriving rulings on when an obligation must be fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of time
Recall that obligations have a defined time (waqt). List the four types: zarf (container), mi'yar (measure), mushtarak (shared), and mushkil (problematic). This lesson focuses on the fourth.
The first three are covered elsewhere; this passage expands on the fourth.
2
Define al-waqt al-mushkil
From the text, al-waqt al-mushkil is time that resembles both a container and a measure. It is 'problematic' because its legal character is ambiguous.
The term 'mushkil' here is not the technical usul term for ambiguous text; it describes the time.
3
Analyze the two aspects using Hajj
First aspect: The time of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) is longer than the actual performance (part of the ten days), so it is a container. Second aspect: Only one Hajj can be performed in that time, making it a measure. Contrast with prayer, where multiple prayers fit in one time.
The text emphasizes that this demonstrates the problematic nature.
4
Note the scope of the concept
The commentary (Al-Qamar) states that this fourth type has no other instance besides Hajj. The use of 'like' (ka) in the text is to allow for possible other examples, but none exist.
This is a unique concept in Hanafi usul.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت
أو يكون مشكلًا يشبه المعيار والظرف كالحج عطف على ما سبق، وهو النوع الرابع من أنواع المؤقت يعني أو يكون وقت المؤقت مشكلاً أي مشتبه الحال يشبه المعيار من وجه، والظرف من وجه ونظيره وقت الحج، فإنه مشكل بهذا المعنى، وذلك من وجهين: الأول: أن وقت الحج: شوال وذو القعدة وعشرة ذي الحجة، والحج لا يؤدى إلا في بعض عشرة ذي الحجة، فيكون الوقت فاضلاً، فمن هذا الوجه يكون ظرفًا، ومن حيث أنه لا يؤدى في هذا الوقت إلا حج واحد يكون معيارا ، بخلاف الصلاة، فإنه في وقت واحد يؤدى صلاة مختلفة، والثاني: أن الحج لا يفرض في العمر إلا مرة واحدة، فإن أدرك العام الثاني والثالث يكون الوقت موسعًا يؤديه في أي وقت شاء، وإن لم يدرك العام الثاني يكون الوقت مضيقًا لابد له أن يؤدي في العام الأول؛ لكن أبا يوسف له اعتبر جانب التضييق ومحمد محله اعتبر جانب التوسع على ما قال المصنف له.
مشكلاً: اسم فاعل من الإشكال بمعنى الاشتباه. (القمر) كالحج التحقيق أن هذا القسم الرابع لا فرد له سوى وقت الحج، فإيراد الكاف نظراً إلى الإمكان الصرف لما عداه. (القمر) على ما سبق: أي على قوله: إما أن يكون الوقت ظرفًا. (القمر) وقت المؤقت إلخ إيماء إلى أن ضمير أو يكون راجع إلى الوقت وجعله راجعا إلى المؤقت كما في "التنوير" لبحر العلوم أي) مولانا عبد العلي لا يخلو عن انتشار، فإن ضمير "يكون" في الجمل السابقة راجع إلى الوقت. (القمر)
أي مشتبه إلخ إيماء إلى أنه ليس المراد في كلام المصنف بالمشكل المشكل الاصطلاحي (القمر) وذلك أي إشكال وقت الحج. (القمر) شوال إلخ فلا يحرم ليحج قبل هذه الأشهر، فلو أحرم قبلها كره تحريما. (القمر) يكون معيارا فيه أن العام الواحد بعض وقت الحج والحج هو الواجب العمري، فكل العمر وقته، وهو فاضل، فلا شائبة فيه للمعيارية، وكون بعض الوقت معيارا لا يستلزم كون جميع الوقت معيارا تأمل. (القمر) يكون الوقت مضيقا إلخ سلمنا أن هذا الوقت مضيق لكن لا يلزم منه كون الوقت للحج معيارا، فإن وقت الحج العمر كله وهو فاضل تأمل. (القمر)

ويتعين أشهر الحج من العام الأول عند أبي يوسف له خلافا لمحمد الله أي لابد عند أبي يوسف له أن يؤدي الحج في العام الأول احتياطاً احتراز عن الفوات، فإن الحياة إلى العام الثاني موهوم والوقت مديد وعند محمد له يترخص له أن يؤخر إلى العام الآخر بشرط أن لا يفوت منه، وثمرة الاختلاف لا تظهر إلا في الإثم، فإذا لم يؤد في العام الأول مردود الشهادة عند أبي يوسف له، ثم إذا أداه في العام الثاني يرتفع عنه الإثم، وتقبل شهادته، وهكذا في كل عام، وعند محمد حله لا يأثم إلا عند الموت، أو إدراك علاماته، ولا يكون مردود الشهادة ولكن كلما أدى يكون أداء عند الفريقين لا قضاء.

لا يقصد النفل مع
Section on the Specific
Explanation of the implication of the command regarding the ruling of time
Or it is problematic, resembling the measure and the container, like Hajj – a conjunction to what preceded, and it is the fourth type of types of time-bound [acts]. That is, the time of the time-bound [act] may be problematic, i.e., ambiguous in state, resembling the measure in one aspect and the container in another aspect. Its example is the time of Hajj, for it is problematic in this sense, from two aspects: First: The time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, and Hajj is only performed during part of the ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Thus the time is surplus, so from this aspect it is a container, and from the aspect that in this time only one Hajj is performed, it is a measure, unlike prayer, for in one time different prayers are performed. Second: Hajj is only obligatory once in a lifetime. If one reaches the second or third year, the time is expansive; he performs it whenever he wishes. If he does not reach the second year, the time is constricted; he must perform it in the first year. But Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) considered the aspect of constriction, and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) considered the aspect of expansion, as the author said for him.
"Mushkilan": active participle from al-ishkal meaning ambiguity. (Al-Qamar) "Like Hajj": the verification is that this fourth category has no instance except the time of Hajj, so the use of the letter kaf is due to the possibility of diverting it to other than it. (Al-Qamar) "Regarding what preceded": i.e., his statement: either the time is a container. (Al-Qamar) "The time of the time-bound [act]" etc.: indicating that the pronoun of "or it is" refers to time, and making it refer to the time-bound as in "Al-Tanwir" of Bahr al-Ulum (i.e.) Mawlana Abd al-Ali is not free from extension, for the pronoun of "is" in the previous sentences refers to time. (Al-Qamar)
"I.e., ambiguous" etc.: indicating that what the author means by al-mushkil is not the technical muskil. (Al-Qamar) "That": i.e., the ambiguity of the time of Hajj. (Al-Qamar) "Shawwal" etc.: so one should not consecrate (ihram) to perform Hajj before these months; if one consecrates before them, it is prohibitively disliked. (Al-Qamar) "Becomes a measure" in it: the same year is part of the time of Hajj, and Hajj is the lifelong obligation, so all of one's life is its time, and it is surplus; thus there is no trace of measurability in it, and the fact that part of the time is a measure does not necessitate that all of the time is a measure; consider. (Al-Qamar) "The time is constricted" etc.: we grant that this time is constricted, but it does not necessarily follow that the time for Hajj is a measure, for the time of Hajj is the whole life, and it is surplus; consider. (Al-Qamar)

The months of Hajj are specifically determined from the first year according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), contrary to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). That is, according to Abu Yusuf, he must perform Hajj in the first year as a precaution, guarding against missing it, for life until the second year is uncertain and the time is prolonged. According to Muhammad, he is permitted to delay it to the other year on condition that it not be missed. The fruit of the disagreement appears only in sin. So if he does not perform it in the first year, his testimony is rejected according to Abu Yusuf, then if he performs it in the second year, the sin is removed from him and his testimony is accepted, and so on each year. According to Muhammad, he does not sin except at death or the appearance of its signs, and his testimony is not rejected. However, whenever he performs it, it is a valid fulfillment (ada') according to both groups, not a makeup (qada').
He becomes
wicked (fasiq)
And it is fulfilled with an absolute intention, not with the intention of supererogatory (nafl). This is from the ruling of its being problematic: i.e., if he performs Hajj with an absolute intention of obligatory Hajj – by saying, "I intend Hajj" – it falls as obligatory, unlike if he says, "I intend supererogatory Hajj." 
"As a precaution": indicating that specifying the months of Hajj from the first year according to Imam Abu Yusuf is for precaution, and it is not based on the view that the command is immediate (fawr) as al-Karkhi said. How so? For if the command in his view were immediate, sin would be entailed by delay, and it would not be removed at all, even if he performed it in the second year, but the matter is not so, as will come. (Al-Qamar)
"He is permitted"
"He is permitted" etc., using as evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Hajj in the tenth year of the Hijra, and the obligation of Hajj was revealed before that, so it is known that delay is permissible. The excuse for Abu Yusuf is that delay is only prohibited due to missing it, and that is because of uncertainty about life, and that is removed in his case, because his life was certain until he taught people the rites of Hajj, and this is not established for others. (Al-Qamar)
"He becomes"
"wicked" etc.: This is not correct, for the basis of what Imam Abu Yusuf said is precaution, which is a speculative proof. So delay beyond the first year is a minor sin, not a major one. For a major sin is established by a definitive proof, and by committing a minor sin once, wickedness (fisq) does not result unless one persists in it. So if he delays it for years, he becomes wicked and his testimony is rejected. This is stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (Al-Qamar) "Except at death" etc.: It is narrated in al-Tahqiq from Abu al-Fadl al-Kirmani that the correct view from Muhammad's statement is that if he dies before performing Hajj, if death is sudden, no sin is incurred upon him. But if death occurs after the appearance of signs that his heart testifies that if he delays further it will be missed, then delay is not permissible for him, and the time becomes constricted upon him due to the existence of evidence, for acting on the evidence of the heart is obligatory in the absence of performance. (Al-Qamar) "It falls as obligatory": because it is apparent that a man with this severe difficulty and with Hajj obligatory upon him, his state indicates that he intends the obligatory. (Al-Qamar)
He does not intend supererogatory with...
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary defines the fourth type of time for religious obligations: the problematic time (al-waqt al-mushkil). The author explains that this time resembles both a container (zarf) – because it has surplus time beyond the actual performance – and a measure (mi'yar) – because only one specific act (Hajj) can be performed within it. The prime example is the time for Hajj. The text then delves into a dispute between the two leading Hanafi scholars, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding whether the obligation of Hajj must be performed immediately in the first available year or can be delayed. Abu Yusuf emphasizes precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid missing the obligation due to the uncertainty of life, while Muhammad allows delay based on the Prophet's own delay in performing Hajj after its obligation. The consequences of this disagreement affect sin and the acceptance of testimony. The commentary (Al-Qamar) clarifies that Abu Yusuf's ruling is not based on the principle of immediate obligation (fawr) but on precaution. Additionally, the text rules that if one intends Hajj in general, it counts as obligatory, not supererogatory, due to the context of the person being obligated.

Key Terms
الوقت المشكل (al-waqt al-mushkil): The time for an obligation that resembles both a container (surplus time) and a measure (only one act fits), like the time for Hajj.
المعيار (al-mi'yar): A measure: the time is exactly sufficient for one specific act, with no surplus.
الظرف (al-zarf): A container: the time has surplus beyond the actual act, like the months of Hajj while the act is only in ten days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is prayer time NOT considered al-waqt al-mushkil according to the passage?
A) Because prayer time is shorter than Hajj time.
B) Because multiple prayers can be performed in the same time slot.
C) Because prayer is obligatory more than once a day.
D) Because prayer does not have a specified time.

Key Takeaway
Al-waqt al-mushkil is a unique time type combining container and measure, with Hajj as its sole exemplar in Hanafi usul.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Internal Hanafi Dispute: Immediate vs. Delayed Hajj
Discusses the internal Hanafi dispute on the timing of Hajj obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the timing of Hajj, their proofs, and the practical consequences regarding sin and testimony.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf: Hajj must be in the first year (precaution); Muhammad: delay is allowed until death signs appear.

In the previous lesson, we learned that the time for Hajj is problematic because it combines container and measure aspects. This leads to a crucial internal Hanafi dispute: must Hajj be performed immediately upon becoming obligatory, or can it be delayed? Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that it must be performed in the first year as a precaution (ihtiyat) against missing it due to death. Muhammad al-Shaybani (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that delay is permissible, citing the Prophet's own delay in performing Hajj. This lesson examines their arguments and the practical implications for sin and legal testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Yusuf: The months of Hajj are specified from the first year; one must perform Hajj in the first year as a precaution. Muhammad: It is permissible to delay to later years, as long as it is performed before death.
Both are Hanafi imams; this is an internal ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the proof for Muhammad's position
Muhammad argues from the Prophet's Sunnah: the Prophet performed Hajj in year 10 AH, while the obligation was revealed earlier. The delay shows that it is permissible to postpone.
The proof is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it yields a speculative ruling.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's argument
Abu Yusuf argues from precaution (ihtiyat): life is uncertain; one might die before the next year, so performing it immediately ensures the obligation is fulfilled.
The commentary clarifies that this is not based on the principle of fawr (immediacy), but on precaution against loss.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Abu Yusuf, delaying beyond the first year incurs a minor sin (not major), and if one persists for years, he becomes a fasiq (wicked) and his testimony is rejected. According to Muhammad, no sin is incurred until death signs appear, and testimony remains accepted.
The sin is minor because the evidence is speculative (zanni).
5
Note the nuances in each view
The commentary (Al-Qamar) adds that even in Abu Yusuf's view, if one performs Hajj in the second year, the sin is removed and testimony is accepted. In Muhammad's view, if death signs appear, delay becomes sinful.
The two views converge at the extreme: both agree that at the point of death or its signs, Hajj must be done immediately.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت
أو يكون مشكلًا يشبه المعيار والظرف كالحج عطف على ما سبق، وهو النوع الرابع من أنواع المؤقت يعني أو يكون وقت المؤقت مشكلاً أي مشتبه الحال يشبه المعيار من وجه، والظرف من وجه ونظيره وقت الحج، فإنه مشكل بهذا المعنى، وذلك من وجهين: الأول: أن وقت الحج: شوال وذو القعدة وعشرة ذي الحجة، والحج لا يؤدى إلا في بعض عشرة ذي الحجة، فيكون الوقت فاضلاً، فمن هذا الوجه يكون ظرفًا، ومن حيث أنه لا يؤدى في هذا الوقت إلا حج واحد يكون معيارا ، بخلاف الصلاة، فإنه في وقت واحد يؤدى صلاة مختلفة، والثاني: أن الحج لا يفرض في العمر إلا مرة واحدة، فإن أدرك العام الثاني والثالث يكون الوقت موسعًا يؤديه في أي وقت شاء، وإن لم يدرك العام الثاني يكون الوقت مضيقًا لابد له أن يؤدي في العام الأول؛ لكن أبا يوسف له اعتبر جانب التضييق ومحمد محله اعتبر جانب التوسع على ما قال المصنف له.
مشكلاً: اسم فاعل من الإشكال بمعنى الاشتباه. (القمر) كالحج التحقيق أن هذا القسم الرابع لا فرد له سوى وقت الحج، فإيراد الكاف نظراً إلى الإمكان الصرف لما عداه. (القمر) على ما سبق: أي على قوله: إما أن يكون الوقت ظرفًا. (القمر) وقت المؤقت إلخ إيماء إلى أن ضمير أو يكون راجع إلى الوقت وجعله راجعا إلى المؤقت كما في "التنوير" لبحر العلوم أي) مولانا عبد العلي لا يخلو عن انتشار، فإن ضمير "يكون" في الجمل السابقة راجع إلى الوقت. (القمر)
أي مشتبه إلخ إيماء إلى أنه ليس المراد في كلام المصنف بالمشكل المشكل الاصطلاحي (القمر) وذلك أي إشكال وقت الحج. (القمر) شوال إلخ فلا يحرم ليحج قبل هذه الأشهر، فلو أحرم قبلها كره تحريما. (القمر) يكون معيارا فيه أن العام الواحد بعض وقت الحج والحج هو الواجب العمري، فكل العمر وقته، وهو فاضل، فلا شائبة فيه للمعيارية، وكون بعض الوقت معيارا لا يستلزم كون جميع الوقت معيارا تأمل. (القمر) يكون الوقت مضيقا إلخ سلمنا أن هذا الوقت مضيق لكن لا يلزم منه كون الوقت للحج معيارا، فإن وقت الحج العمر كله وهو فاضل تأمل. (القمر)

ويتعين أشهر الحج من العام الأول عند أبي يوسف له خلافا لمحمد الله أي لابد عند أبي يوسف له أن يؤدي الحج في العام الأول احتياطاً احتراز عن الفوات، فإن الحياة إلى العام الثاني موهوم والوقت مديد وعند محمد له يترخص له أن يؤخر إلى العام الآخر بشرط أن لا يفوت منه، وثمرة الاختلاف لا تظهر إلا في الإثم، فإذا لم يؤد في العام الأول مردود الشهادة عند أبي يوسف له، ثم إذا أداه في العام الثاني يرتفع عنه الإثم، وتقبل شهادته، وهكذا في كل عام، وعند محمد حله لا يأثم إلا عند الموت، أو إدراك علاماته، ولا يكون مردود الشهادة ولكن كلما أدى يكون أداء عند الفريقين لا قضاء.

يترخص
له إلخ مستدلاً بأن النبي حج سنة عشرة من هجرة ونزلت فرضية الحج قبلها فعلم أن التأخير جائز، والعذر لأبي يوسف له أن التأخير إنما حرم للفوات، وذلك بالشك في الحياة، وقد ارتفع ذلك في حقه . لأن حياته كان متيقنا إلى أن يبين الناس أمور الحج وهذا لم يثبت في حق غيره . (القمر)
يصير
فاسقا إلخ: هذا ليس بصحيح، فإن بناء ما قال الإمام أبو يوسف على الاحتياط وهو دليل ظني، فالتأخير عن العام الأول يكون ذنبًا صغيرًا لا كبيرًا، فإن الكبيرة تثبت بدليل قطعي، وبارتكاب الصغيرة مرة، ولا يحصل الفسق إلا إذا أصر عليها، فلو أخر سنين يصير فاسقا مردود الشهادة كذا في "الدر المختار". (القمر) إلا عند الموت إلخ: نقل في "التحقيق" عن أبي الفضل الكرماني: أن الصحيح من قول محمد محله: إنه إذا مات قبل أن يحج، فإن كان الموت فجاءة لم يلحقه إثم، وإن كان بعد ظهور أمارات يشهد قلبه بأنه لو أخر يفوت لم يحل له التأخير، ويصير متضيقاً عليه؛ لقيام الدليل، فإن العمل بدليل القلب واجب عند عدم الأداء. (القمر) يقع عن الفرض: إذ الظاهر أن الرجل مع هذه المحنة الشديدة وعليه فرض الحج، فحاله يدل على أنه يريد الفرض. (القمر)

Section on the Specific
Explanation of the implication of the command regarding the ruling of time
Or it is problematic, resembling the measure and the container, like Hajj – a conjunction to what preceded, and it is the fourth type of types of time-bound [acts]. That is, the time of the time-bound [act] may be problematic, i.e., ambiguous in state, resembling the measure in one aspect and the container in another aspect. Its example is the time of Hajj, for it is problematic in this sense, from two aspects: First: The time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, and Hajj is only performed during part of the ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Thus the time is surplus, so from this aspect it is a container, and from the aspect that in this time only one Hajj is performed, it is a measure, unlike prayer, for in one time different prayers are performed. Second: Hajj is only obligatory once in a lifetime. If one reaches the second or third year, the time is expansive; he performs it whenever he wishes. If he does not reach the second year, the time is constricted; he must perform it in the first year. But Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) considered the aspect of constriction, and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) considered the aspect of expansion, as the author said for him.
"Mushkilan": active participle from al-ishkal meaning ambiguity. (Al-Qamar) "Like Hajj": the verification is that this fourth category has no instance except the time of Hajj, so the use of the letter kaf is due to the possibility of diverting it to other than it. (Al-Qamar) "Regarding what preceded": i.e., his statement: either the time is a container. (Al-Qamar) "The time of the time-bound [act]" etc.: indicating that the pronoun of "or it is" refers to time, and making it refer to the time-bound as in "Al-Tanwir" of Bahr al-Ulum (i.e.) Mawlana Abd al-Ali is not free from extension, for the pronoun of "is" in the previous sentences refers to time. (Al-Qamar)
"I.e., ambiguous" etc.: indicating that what the author means by al-mushkil is not the technical muskil. (Al-Qamar) "That": i.e., the ambiguity of the time of Hajj. (Al-Qamar) "Shawwal" etc.: so one should not consecrate (ihram) to perform Hajj before these months; if one consecrates before them, it is prohibitively disliked. (Al-Qamar) "Becomes a measure" in it: the same year is part of the time of Hajj, and Hajj is the lifelong obligation, so all of one's life is its time, and it is surplus; thus there is no trace of measurability in it, and the fact that part of the time is a measure does not necessitate that all of the time is a measure; consider. (Al-Qamar) "The time is constricted" etc.: we grant that this time is constricted, but it does not necessarily follow that the time for Hajj is a measure, for the time of Hajj is the whole life, and it is surplus; consider. (Al-Qamar)

The months of Hajj are specifically determined from the first year according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), contrary to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). That is, according to Abu Yusuf, he must perform Hajj in the first year as a precaution, guarding against missing it, for life until the second year is uncertain and the time is prolonged. According to Muhammad, he is permitted to delay it to the other year on condition that it not be missed. The fruit of the disagreement appears only in sin. So if he does not perform it in the first year, his testimony is rejected according to Abu Yusuf, then if he performs it in the second year, the sin is removed from him and his testimony is accepted, and so on each year. According to Muhammad, he does not sin except at death or the appearance of its signs, and his testimony is not rejected. However, whenever he performs it, it is a valid fulfillment (ada') according to both groups, not a makeup (qada').
He becomes
wicked (fasiq)
And it is fulfilled with an absolute intention, not with the intention of supererogatory (nafl). This is from the ruling of its being problematic: i.e., if he performs Hajj with an absolute intention of obligatory Hajj – by saying, "I intend Hajj" – it falls as obligatory, unlike if he says, "I intend supererogatory Hajj." 
"As a precaution": indicating that specifying the months of Hajj from the first year according to Imam Abu Yusuf is for precaution, and it is not based on the view that the command is immediate (fawr) as al-Karkhi said. How so? For if the command in his view were immediate, sin would be entailed by delay, and it would not be removed at all, even if he performed it in the second year, but the matter is not so, as will come. (Al-Qamar)
"He is permitted"
"He is permitted" etc., using as evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Hajj in the tenth year of the Hijra, and the obligation of Hajj was revealed before that, so it is known that delay is permissible. The excuse for Abu Yusuf is that delay is only prohibited due to missing it, and that is because of uncertainty about life, and that is removed in his case, because his life was certain until he taught people the rites of Hajj, and this is not established for others. (Al-Qamar)
"He becomes"
"wicked" etc.: This is not correct, for the basis of what Imam Abu Yusuf said is precaution, which is a speculative proof. So delay beyond the first year is a minor sin, not a major one. For a major sin is established by a definitive proof, and by committing a minor sin once, wickedness (fisq) does not result unless one persists in it. So if he delays it for years, he becomes wicked and his testimony is rejected. This is stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (Al-Qamar) "Except at death" etc.: It is narrated in al-Tahqiq from Abu al-Fadl al-Kirmani that the correct view from Muhammad's statement is that if he dies before performing Hajj, if death is sudden, no sin is incurred upon him. But if death occurs after the appearance of signs that his heart testifies that if he delays further it will be missed, then delay is not permissible for him, and the time becomes constricted upon him due to the existence of evidence, for acting on the evidence of the heart is obligatory in the absence of performance. (Al-Qamar) "It falls as obligatory": because it is apparent that a man with this severe difficulty and with Hajj obligatory upon him, his state indicates that he intends the obligatory. (Al-Qamar)

Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary defines the fourth type of time for religious obligations: the problematic time (al-waqt al-mushkil). The author explains that this time resembles both a container (zarf) – because it has surplus time beyond the actual performance – and a measure (mi'yar) – because only one specific act (Hajj) can be performed within it. The prime example is the time for Hajj. The text then delves into a dispute between the two leading Hanafi scholars, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding whether the obligation of Hajj must be performed immediately in the first available year or can be delayed. Abu Yusuf emphasizes precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid missing the obligation due to the uncertainty of life, while Muhammad allows delay based on the Prophet's own delay in performing Hajj after its obligation. The consequences of this disagreement affect sin and the acceptance of testimony. The commentary (Al-Qamar) clarifies that Abu Yusuf's ruling is not based on the principle of immediate obligation (fawr) but on precaution. Additionally, the text rules that if one intends Hajj in general, it counts as obligatory, not supererogatory, due to the context of the person being obligated.

Key Terms
الوقت المشكل (al-waqt al-mushkil): The time for an obligation that resembles both a container (surplus time) and a measure (only one act fits), like the time for Hajj.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precaution: a principle used by Abu Yusuf to require immediate performance to avoid missing the obligation.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement, here affecting sin and testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad's position, when does a person become sinful for delaying Hajj?
A) As soon as he delays beyond the first year.
B) Only when he dies without performing it.
C) Only at the point of death or when death signs appear.
D) He never becomes sinful because Hajj can be performed at any time.

Key Takeaway
The internal Hanafi dispute on Hajj's timing shows how speculation (zann) leads to differences in sin and testimony, while both views uphold the validity of the act.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Timing of Obligation: Fawr vs. Tarakhi in the Hajj Command
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the implication of the Hajj command regarding time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between immediate (fawr) and deferred (tarakhi) performance to a command, using the Hajj dispute as a case study.

Core Idea
A command does not inherently require immediate performance; delay is permitted unless evidence of forfeiture exists.

The obligation of Hajj was revealed in Medina, yet the Prophet performed it in year 10 AH. Did the command require immediate performance in the first year, or was delay allowed? This question sparked an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, each bringing different proofs and practical consequences. Their debate illustrates a core usul principle about the nature of commands and the role of precaution (ihtiyat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is the obligation of Hajj. The dispute is whether it must be performed in the first possible year or can be delayed to later years.
Both agree Hajj is obligatory, but differ on the implication of the command regarding time.
2
Understand each imam's reasoning and evidence
Abu Yusuf: performance in the first year as precaution (ihtiyat) against missing it due to uncertain life. Muhammad: delay is permissible, citing the Prophet's Hajj in year 10 after the obligation was revealed.
The evidence for Muhammad is a Sunnah (prophetic action); for Abu Yusuf, it is a rational principle of precaution.
3
Analyze the thamarah (practical consequence)
Under Abu Yusuf, delay causes sin and rejection of testimony, removed upon performance. Under Muhammad, sin only at death or its signs, and testimony is not rejected.
Both agree that later performance is ada' (timely performance), not qada' (make-up).
4
Recognize the refinement by later commentators
Al-Qamar clarifies that Abu Yusuf's position is based on ihtiyat, not on a view that the command is for fawr. The sin from delay is minor; fisq only arises from persistence. Muhammad's position is refined by al-Kirmani regarding sudden death versus signs of death.
This shows how later scholars clarified and nuanced the positions.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت ويتعين أشهر الحج من العام الأول عند أبي يوسف له خلافا لمحمد الله أي لابد عند أبي يوسف له أن يؤدي الحج في العام الأول احتياطاً احتراز عن الفوات، فإن الحياة إلى العام الثاني موهوم والوقت مديد وعند محمد له يترخص له أن يؤخر إلى العام الآخر بشرط أن لا يفوت منه، وثمرة الاختلاف لا تظهر إلا في الإثم، فإذا لم يؤد في العام الأول مردود الشهادة عند أبي يوسف له، ثم إذا أداه في العام الثاني يرتفع عنه الإثم، وتقبل شهادته، وهكذا في كل عام، وعند محمد حله لا يأثم إلا عند الموت، أو إدراك علاماته، ولا يكون مردود الشهادة ولكن كلما أدى يكون أداء عند الفريقين لا قضاء. يصير فاسقا احتياطاً: إيماء إلى أن تعيين أشهر الحج من العام الأول عند الإمام أبي يوسف الله للاحتياط، وليس مبنيا على أن الأمر عنده للفور كما قال الكرخي، كيف ولو كان الأمر عنده للفور للزم الإثم عند التأخير، ولا يرتفع أصلاً، وإن أدى في العام الثاني مع أن الأمر ليس كذلك على ما سيجيء. (القمر) يترخص له إلخ مستدلاً بأن النبي حج سنة عشرة من هجرة ونزلت فرضية الحج قبلها فعلم أن التأخير جائز، والعذر لأبي يوسف له أن التأخير إنما حرم للفوات، وذلك بالشك في الحياة، وقد ارتفع ذلك في حقه . لأن حياته كان متيقنا إلى أن يبين الناس أمور الحج وهذا لم يثبت في حق غيره . (القمر) يصير فاسقا إلخ: هذا ليس بصحيح، فإن بناء ما قال الإمام أبو يوسف على الاحتياط وهو دليل ظني، فالتأخير عن العام الأول يكون ذنبًا صغيرًا لا كبيرًا، فإن الكبيرة تثبت بدليل قطعي، وبارتكاب الصغيرة مرة، ولا يحصل الفسق إلا إذا أصر عليها، فلو أخر سنين يصير فاسقا مردود الشهادة كذا في "الدر المختار". (القمر) إلا عند الموت إلخ: نقل في "التحقيق" عن أبي الفضل الكرماني: أن الصحيح من قول محمد محله: إنه إذا مات قبل أن يحج، فإن كان الموت فجاءة لم يلحقه إثم، وإن كان بعد ظهور أمارات يشهد قلبه بأنه لو أخر يفوت لم يحل له التأخير، ويصير متضيقاً عليه؛ لقيام الدليل، فإن العمل بدليل القلب واجب عند عدم الأداء. (القمر)
Explanation of the requirement of the command regarding the ruling of time: The months of Hajj are determined from the first year according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, meaning that according to Abu Yusuf he must perform Hajj in the first year as a precaution against missing it, because life until the second year is uncertain and the time is long. According to Muhammad, he may delay to the next year provided that it is not missed. The fruit of the difference appears only in sin: if he does not perform in the first year, his testimony is rejected according to Abu Yusuf; then if he performs in the second year, the sin is removed and his testimony is accepted, and so on every year. According to Muhammad, he does not sin except at death or upon perceiving its signs, and his testimony is not rejected, but whenever he performs it is an ada' (performance) according to both, not qada' (make-up). He becomes a fasiq. 'As a precaution': indicating that specifying the months of Hajj from the first year according to Imam Abu Yusuf is for precaution, not based on his view that the command is immediate as al-Karkhi said. 'He may delay etc.' using as proof that the Prophet performed Hajj in the tenth year of Hijra while the obligation of Hajj was revealed before that, so delay is permissible. The excuse for Abu Yusuf is that delay is prohibited only due to the possibility of missing it, and that arises from uncertainty about life, which is removed in his case because his life was certain until he explained the matters of Hajj to people, and this is not established for others. 'He becomes a fasiq etc.': This is not correct, for the basis of what Imam Abu Yusuf said is precaution, which is a speculative proof, so delay beyond the first year is a minor sin, not a major one; major sins are established by definitive proof, and committing a minor sin once does not cause fisq unless one persists. 'Except at death etc.': It is transmitted in al-Tahqiq from Abu al-Fadl al-Kirmani that the correct view of Muhammad is that if he dies before performing Hajj, if death is sudden he incurs no sin, but if after signs that his heart testifies that if he delays it will be missed, delay is not permissible for him and it becomes restricted upon him due to the existence of evidence, for acting upon the evidence of the heart is obligatory in case of non-performance.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage examines the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the time of performing the obligatory Hajj. The base text states that the months of Hajj are determined from the first year for Abu Yusuf, who requires immediate performance in the first year as a precaution (ihtiyat) against missing the obligation due to the uncertainty of life. Muhammad allows delay to the second year provided the obligation is not missed. The practical difference (thamarah) is in sin and legal testimony: under Abu Yusuf, delaying past the first year causes sin and rejection of testimony, but performance in the second year removes the sin and restores testimony. Under Muhammad, sin only occurs at death or when death signs appear, and testimony is not rejected. The commentary by al-Qamar refines the understanding: Abu Yusuf's position is based on precaution, not on the view that the command is immediate (fawr). The annotation clarifies that the sin from delay is minor, not major, and fisq (transgression leading to rejection of testimony) only occurs from persistence. Another annotation discusses Muhammad's view further, citing al-Kirmani that sudden death before Hajj incurs no sin, but if signs of death appear, delay becomes impermissible. This passage illustrates how Hanafi usul analyzes the implication of a command (amr) regarding time, distinguishing between immediate and delayed performance, and how the authority of the ruling relates to precautionary principles.

Key Terms
فور (fawr): Immediate performance of an obligation upon the command, without delay.
تراخي (tarakhi): Permissible delay in performing a commanded act, as long as the obligation is not missed.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary measure to avoid potential sin or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah) of delaying Hajj beyond the first year according to Abu Yusuf?
A) No sin, and testimony is accepted.
B) Sin and rejection of testimony until the Hajj is performed.
C) Sin but testimony is not rejected.
D) The Hajj becomes invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a command does not inherently require immediate performance; the timing depends on contextual evidence and precaution.

Intention for Hajj: Absolute vs. Nafl
Ruling on intention for Hajj with absolute vs. nafl niyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that explicit intention overrides implied intent and explain the qiyas reasoning comparing Hajj to fasting and prayer.

Core Idea
Explicit nafl intention overrides obligation; Hajj resembles fasting (absolute intent suffices) and prayer (nafl intent stays nafl).

This passage explores a subtle point of intention (niyyah) for Hajj. How do we determine whether a pilgrim's pilgrimage counts as the obligatory Hajj or a voluntary one? The Hanafi school gives primacy to the explicit wording, while the Shafi'i school argues for a default interpretation based on the pilgrim's state. The text resolves this through a dual analogy that illuminates the nature of Hajj as both a measure of devotion and a time-bound container of actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Exception
Start by reading the first sentence: the base rule is that absolute intention (saying 'I intend Hajj') discharges the obligation, but explicit nafl intention does not become fard. Note the two scenarios.
The exception is the entire point of the passage.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i Objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that a person who owes Hajj but intends nafl is foolish and should be placed under legal restriction (hajr), meaning his action should be treated as fard. Understand the logic: obligation weakens choice.
Hajr normally applies to financial matters, not worship.
3
Examine the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi reply: restricting choice invalidates the condition of free will (ikhtiyar) required in worship. Explicit intention is paramount; the state does not override words.
This reflects the usul principle: al-umur bi-maqasidiha but explicit niyyah is decisive.
4
Unpack the Qiyas Reasoning
The text compares Hajj to two acts: fasting (a 'standard' – mi'yar) where absolute intention suffices for fard, and prayer (a 'container' – zarf) where explicit nafl intention remains nafl. Hajj shares both aspects, so the ruling is two-part.
This is qiyas jaliy: the illa is the shared attribute (measure or container).
5
Derive the Usul Principle
The operative principle: explicit intention overrides implied context in acts of worship. Choice (ikhtiyar) is a condition for validity; legal restrictions (hajr) do not apply to worship to negate choice.
This is a key distinction between ibadat and muamalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتأدى بإطلاق النية لا بنية النفل هذا من حكم كونه مشكلاً أي إن أدى الحج بمطلق الحج الفرض النية بأن يقول: نويت الحج يقع عن الفرض، بخلاف ما إذا قال: "نويت حج النفل"، يقع عن النفل: إذ الظاهر أن الرجل مع هذه المحنة الشديدة وعليه فرض الحج، فحاله يدل على أنه يريد الفرض. (القمر) لا يقصد النفل مع فإنه يقع عن النفل، وقال الشافعي : يقع ههنا عن الفرض أيضًا؛ لأنه سفيه يجب أن يحجر عليه، ولا يقبل تصرفه، قلنا: هذا يبطل الاختيار الذي شرط في العبادات. الحجر والحاصل أن الحج لما كان يشبه المعيار والظرف أخذ شبهاً من كل منهما، فمن حيث كونه معياراً أخذ شبهاً من الصوم فيتأدى مطلق النية كالصوم، ومن حيث كونه ظرفاً أخذ شبهاً من الصلاة، فلا يتأدى بنية النفل كالصلاة هكذا ينبغى أن يفهم.
And it is performed with absolute intention, not with intention of nafl. This is due to its being ambiguous: if he performs Hajj with an absolute intention for Hajj as fard by saying 'I intend Hajj', it counts for fard, contrary to if he says 'I intend nafl Hajj'. It counts as nafl: because the apparent situation is that the person is in severe difficulty and has an obligatory Hajj, so his state indicates he intends the fard. (al-Qamar) He does not intend nafl along with it, for it would count as nafl. Al-Shafi'i said: here it counts as fard as well, because he is foolish and should be placed under restriction (hajr), and his actions are not accepted. We said: this invalidates the choice that is a condition in acts of worship. The restriction. The conclusion is that Hajj resembles both a standard and a container, taking resemblance from each: in being a standard, it resembles fasting, so it is performed with absolute intention like fasting; in being a container, it resembles prayer, so it is not performed with intention of nafl like prayer. This is how it should be understood.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of intention (niyyah) when performing the obligatory Hajj. The base ruling: if a person upon whom Hajj is obligatory performs the pilgrimage with an absolute intention (simply saying 'I intend Hajj'), it counts as the fard (obligatory) Hajj, not as nafl (supererogatory). However, if he explicitly intends nafl by saying 'I intend nafl Hajj', it counts as nafl, even if he owes the fard. This is because the time and his situation (being obligated) indicate that he likely intends the fard. The commentary raises an objection: if he intends nafl, his intention is explicit, so it should be nafl. The Shafi'i school argues that since he is under obligation and foolish to do nafl instead of fard, he should be placed under legal restriction (hajr), and his nafl intention should be overridden to count as fard. The Hanafi response is that this would negate the element of choice (ikhtiyar) that is essential in worship. The passage then provides an analogy: Hajj resembles both a standard (mi'yar) like fasting, where absolute intention suffices for the obligatory, and a container (zarf) like prayer, where explicit intention of nafl does not count as fard. Therefore, similar to fasting, if one intends without specifying, it counts as fard; but if he explicitly intends nafl, it remains nafl, like in prayer. This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that explicit intention overrides implicit intent, and that ikhtiyar is fundamental in worship.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; determines the type of worship, whether fard or nafl.
حجر (hajr): Legal restriction preventing a person from executing financial or religious actions due to foolishness.
اختيار (ikhtiyar): Free choice; a condition for validity of acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle illustrated in this lesson, what is the ruling if a person who owes the fard Hajj says 'I intend nafl Hajj'?
A) It counts as fard because he is obligated and his state indicates he needs to fulfill it.
B) It counts as nafl, and he still owes the fard.
C) The Hajj is invalid because of the contradiction.
D) It counts as fard only if he is under legal restriction (hajr).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, explicit intention determines the nature of worship; nafl intention cannot be overridden by obligation, because choice is a condition for the validity of ibadat.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Hanafi Position on Disbelievers and Worship Obligations
Dispute on whether disbelievers are addressed with worship performance in this world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether disbelievers are addressed with acts of worship, and evaluate the opposing view using the hadith of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are not obligated to perform worship that can be dropped, because obligation follows faith.

This lesson examines a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh: are disbelievers (kuffār) addressed by the commands of sharī‘ah to perform acts of worship in this world? The Hanafī school holds a nuanced position distinguishing between acts that can be dropped (like prayer and fasting) and those that cannot (like faith). We will explore the evidence from the hadith of Mu‘ādh and the opposing view of al-Shāfi‘ī.

Guided Path
1
Define the question
Identify the precise legal issue: Are disbelievers (kuffār) legally obligated (mukhaṭab) to perform acts of worship in this world, or is the obligation contingent upon faith?
This is a dispute about taklīf (legal responsibility).
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the majority of Hanafī scholars (Transoxania), disbelievers are not addressed with acts of worship that can be dropped (e.g., prayer, fasting), because such acts are not obligatory without faith.
The criterion: 'mā yaḥtamil al-suqūṭ' – acts that can fall away under certain conditions (e.g., menstruation) are not obligatory on disbelievers.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith of Mu‘ādh is the key proof. The Prophet first called to faith, then to prayer only after obedience to faith. This shows worship obligations are contingent upon prior faith.
The hadith is narrated in multiple authentic collections (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.) and is considered clear (nass) on this condition.
4
Present the opposing view
Al-Shāfi‘ī and some Iraqi mashāyikh hold that disbelievers are addressed with all commands, including worship. They cite Quranic verses that punish for abandoning prayer and zakat.
They interpret general commands (e.g., 'Aqimū al-ṣalāh') as addressing all, including disbelievers.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and thamarah
The Hanafīs respond that the Quranic evidence is open to metaphorical interpretation, while the hadith is explicit. The practical consequence (thamarah): if a disbeliever prays before embracing Islam, according to Hanafīs the prayer is not valid and no make-up is required; according to Shāfi‘īs it is valid but not required.
This shows how the usul dispute directly affects fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث الخاص
بيان موجب الأمر في حق الكفار
أي لم نك من المعتقدين للصلاة المفروضة، والزكاة المفروضة هكذا قالوا، وقد فسرته في "التفسير الأحمدي" بأطنب وجه وأشمله.
وأما في وجوب الأداء في أحكام الدنيا فكذلك عند البعض يعني أنهم مخاطبون بأداء العبادات في الدنيا أيضا عند البعض من مشايخ العراق، وأكثر أصحاب الشافعي حبه، وهذه مغلطة عظيمة للقوم؛ لأن الشافعي لم يقل بصحة أدائها منهم حالة الكفر، ولا بوجوب قضائها بعد الإسلام، فما معنى وجوب الأداء في الدنيا، فلذا أوّلوا كلامه بأن معنى الخطاب في حقهم آمنوا ثم صلوا، فيقدر الإيمان مقتضى تبعًا للعبادات، وثمرته أنهم يؤاخذون عنده في الآخرة بترك فعل الصلاة كما يعذبون بترك اعتقادها اتفاقا، فلو لم يكونوا مخاطبين بأداء العبادات أي لم نك إلخ فيه أن هذا المعنى مجازي، والمجاز لا يثبت إلا بدليل، وأما ظاهر الآية فيدل على أن الكفار يعذبون بترك فعل الصلاة والزكاة فهو حجة للشافعي لله ومشايخ العراق، وقال بحر العلوم إن التأويل بالصلاة الواجبة والزكاة الواجبة بعيد، فإن الآية مكية، والزكاة إنما فرضت بالمدينة وما سواها من الإطعام مندوب، فكيف ينتهض سببًا لسلوك النار بل سبب سلوكهم كونهم كافرين وبينوا كفرهم بالكناية أي ذكر لوازمه وأماراته، والمعنى والله أعلم. ما تسألون عن سلوكنا النار مع أنه لم يكن فبينا علامة من علامات المؤمنين من الصلاة والإطعام بل علامات الكفار، والخوض معهم، وتكذيب يوم الدين، إلا أن يثبت وجوب صدقة ما سوى الزكاة قبل الهجرة فحينئذ يكون لهذا الاستدلال وجه. (القمر) وقد فسرته إلخ ليس في التفسير "الأحمدي" أمر زائد في هذا المبحث على ما في هذا الشرح، ولذا ما نقلت عبارته . (القمر) وأكثر أصحاب الشافعي والشافعي كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) أدائها إلخ ضميره وكذا ضمير قضائها راجع إلى العبادات (القمر) كلامه: أي كلام الشافعي وهو مخاطبون بأداء العبادات في الدنيا. (القمر) فيقدر إلخ لا يقال: إن الإيمان رأس الطاعات، فكيف يثبت وجوبه تبعًا للعبادات؛ لأنا نقول : إن وجوب الإيمان ثابت بالأوامر المستقلة فهو ثابت عبارة واقتضاء ولا محذور فيه، إنما المحذور لو لم يكن ثبوته عبارة (القمر) مقتضى إلخ فإن الإيمان شرط لأداء جميع العبادات، وهذا كما أن الجنب يجب عليه الصلاة بشرط الطهارة، فكذا يجب على الكفار العبادات بشرط الإيمان.
