بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث
بحث الواو
في قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللَّهِ﴾، ففهم النبي عليه منه الترتيب، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا﴾ فإن تقديم الركوع على السجود واجب.
والجواب عن الأول: أن النبي عليه لعله فهم الترتيب من وحي غير متلو، وإنما أحال على الآية باعتبار أن التقديم في الذكر لا يخلو عن الاهتمام والترجيح.
وعن الثاني: أنه معارض لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْجُدِي وَارْكَعِي﴾ خطابًا لمريم، فإن تقديم السجود على الركوع ليس بفرض بالإجماع.
إن الصفا والمروة إلخ الصفا في الأصل الحجر الصلب سمي به ذلك المكان الشريف؛ لأنه حجر صلب، وروي أن آدم عليه نزل عليه فاشتق له قلت والعامة القائلون بعدم الترتيب يحتجون بقول العرب جاءني زيد وعمرو فيما جاءا متقارنين أو متعاقبين بصفة الوصل أو بصفة التراخي على الإطلاق، ثبت ذلك بالنقل عن أئمة اللغة، وقد نص عليه سيبويه في سبعة عشر مواضع من كتابه، وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ﴾ إلخ، فلا يوجب الترتيب أيضا، ألا ترى أن المراد بالآية إثبات أنهما من شعائر الله ولا يتصور فيه الترتيب، وإنما أوجب النبي فيه الترتيب؛ لأن السعي لا ينفك عن الترتيب المعين، فعينه من الصفا؛ لأن التقديم في الذكر من أسباب الترجيح.
(السنبلي) من شعائر الله : جمع الشعيرة أي العلامة أي من علامات عبادات الله تعالى.
(القمر) ففهم إلخ والنبي عليه كان أعلم العرب والعجم وأفصح منهما.
وقوله تعالى: ﴿ارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا﴾ إلخ قلت وأجاب عن هذا الدليل بحر العلوم والفنون بأنه قال: لا نسلم أنه فهم الترتيب في الركوع والسجود من هذه الكريمة، بل فهم من قوله : "صلوا كما رأيتموني أصلي"، فهذا الأمر هدانا إلى وجوب الترتيب ثم قال: لكن دلالة هذا الحديث على وجوب الترتيب من الركوع والسجود محل تأمل، فإذن الأصلح التمسك بما قد وقع في حديث الأعرابي الذي ورد لبيان حقيقة الصلاة بكلمة "ثم".
(السنبلي) إنه معارض إلخ فعلم أن المقصود في الآيتين الأمر بالركنين أي الركوع والسجود، وأما الترتيب فله دليل آخر.
(القمر) أخرجه مسلم في "صحيحه"، رقم: 1218، باب حجة النبي والنسائي، رقم: 2961، باب القول بعد ركعتي الطواف وأبو داود رقم: 1905، باب صفة حجة النبي، وابن ماجه، رقم: 3074، باب حجة رسول الله، وأحمد في مسنده، رقم: 1448، وابن حبان في صحيحه رقم 3943، 9/251، عن جابر بهذا اللفظ، وفي رواية للنسائي، رقم: 2962 باب القول بعد ركعتي الطواف والدار قطني، 2/254، عن جابر، فابدؤوا بما بدأ الله به.
(المحشي) وفي قوله لغير الموطوءة: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وطالق وطالق"، جواب سؤال مقدر يرد علينا وهو أنه إذا قال أحد لامرأته الغير الموطوءة: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وطالق وطالق" فعند أبي حنيفة لم تقع واحدة وعندهما: ثلاث فعلم أن الواو للترتيب عنده، فيقع الأول منفردًا ولم يبق المحل للثاني والثالث، وللمقارنة عندهما فيقع الكل دفعة واحدة، والمحل يقبلها، فأجاب بأن في هذا المثال إنما تطلق واحدة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله؛ لأن موجب هذا الكلام الافتراق فلا يتغير بالواو، وقالا موجبه الاجتماع، فلا يتغير بالواو يعني أن هذا الترتيب عنده والمقارنة عندهما لم يجئ من الواو، بل من موجب الكلام، فإن موجب الكلام عنده الافتراق؛ إذ لو لم يكن كذلك لقال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثلاثا، فإذا لم يقل: ثلاثًا بل قال: أنت طالق وطالق وطالق علم أنه قصد الافتراق، فيقع كلّ منها على حدة، فيقع الأول ولم يبق محل للثاني وللثالث، وعندهما: موجب الكلام الاجتماع؛ لأنه لو لم يكن كذلك لما علق الثلاث كله بشرط واحد، فإذا علقه جملة وقع جملة واحدة، وقد مال فخر الإسلام وصاحب "التقويم" لغير الموطوءة إنما قال: هذا؛ لأن المرأة إذا كانت مدخولة، وقيل لها: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق طالق طالق"، تقع الثلاثة بالاتفاق بعد وجود الشرط؛ لكونها محلاً لها.
(القمر) فيقع الأول: أي يقع الطلقة الأولى وبانت بواحدة؛ لكونها غير مدخولة بها، ولا عدة لغير الموطوءة، فلم تبق محلاً للثاني والثالث، وهذا هو الترتيب؛ إذ لو لم يكن الواو للترتيب عنده، وكانت لمطلق الجمع لكان ينبغي أن يقع الطلقات الثلاث عند وجود الشرط.
(القمر) فلا يتغير إلخ فإن الواو لمطلق الجمع، وهو متحقق في الافتراق أيضًا.
(القمر) فلا يتغير إلخ لأن الواو لمطلق الجمع، وهو متحقق في الاجتماع أيضًا.
(القمر) لم يجئ فإن الإمام وصاحبيه متفقون على أن الواو لمطلق الجمع.
(القمر) وقد مال إلخ اعلم أولاً أن الترتيب عند الإمام إنما ثبت بموجب الكلام وضرورته لا بموجب الواو، والضرورة هي أن قوله: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق" جملة تامة لا تحتاج إلى ما بعدها وأما قوله "وطالق وطالق" فجملة ناقصة، فيتوقف على الجملة الأولى لا محالة، إذ الناقصة مفتقرة إلى الكاملة في إفادة المعنى؛ إذ لو لم يكن العطف لما أفادت
Statement of the sections of the third division. Discussion of the conjunction 'wa'. Regarding His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah', the Prophet understood from it order. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Bow and prostrate', thus the precedence of bowing over prostration is obligatory. The answer to the first: the Prophet perhaps understood the order from unrecited revelation, and he only referred to the verse on the basis that precedence in mention is not devoid of emphasis and weighting. And regarding the second: it is opposed by His statement, the Exalted: 'And prostrate and bow', addressed to Maryam, for the precedence of prostration over bowing is not obligatory by consensus. 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah' etc. as-Safa originally means hard stone; that noble place was named because it is hard stone, and it is narrated that Adam descended upon it... and the general body of scholars who deny order argue with the statement of the Arabs: 'Zaid came to me and Amr' meaning they came together or successively with the attribute of conjunction or with the attribute of delay absolutely, that is established by transmission from the imams of language, and Sibawayh stated it in seventeen places of his book. As for His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah' etc., it does not necessitate order either, don't you see that the intent of the verse is to establish that both are among the symbols of Allah and order is not conceivable in that? Rather, the Prophet made order obligatory because the Sa'y is inseparable from a specific order, so he specified it from as-Safa because precedence in mention is a cause for weighting. (al-Sunbuli) 'Among the symbols of Allah': plural of sha'ira i.e. sign, i.e. among the signs of the worship of Allah, the Exalted. (al-Qamar) 'He understood' etc. and the Prophet was the most knowledgeable of Arabs and non-Arabs and the most eloquent of them. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Bow and prostrate' etc. I said and answered this proof Bahr al-Ulum wa al-Funun by saying: we do not concede that he understood order in bowing and prostration from this noble verse; rather, he understood it from his statement: 'Pray as you have seen me praying', thus this command guided us to the obligation of order. Then he said: but the indication of this hadith to the obligation of order in bowing and prostration is a place for contemplation; therefore the most correct is to adhere to what has occurred in the hadith of the Bedouin which came to explain the reality of prayer with the word 'thumma'. (al-Sunbuli) 'It is opposed' etc. So it is known that the purpose in the two verses is the command of the two pillars i.e. bowing and prostration; as for order, there is another proof for it. (al-Qamar) Extracted by Muslim in his Sahih, no. 1218, chapter of the Hajj of the Prophet; al-Nasa'i, no. 2961, chapter of the statement after the two rak'ahs of Tawaf; Abu Dawud, no. 1905, chapter of the description of the Hajj of the Prophet; Ibn Majah, no. 3074, chapter of the Hajj of the Messenger of Allah; Ahmad in his Musnad, no. 1448; Ibn Hibban in his Sahih, no. 3943, 9/251, from Jabir with this wording, and in a narration of al-Nasa'i, no. 2962, chapter of the statement after the two rak'ahs of Tawaf; al-Daraqutni, 2/254, from Jabir: 'Start with what Allah started with.' (al-Muhashi) And in his statement to the non-consummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced', it is an answer to an implied objection that comes to us: if a man says to his non-consummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced', according to Abu Hanifa, nothing occurs? [correction: one divorce occurs] and according to them both, three occur. So it is known that 'wa' indicates order according to him, so the first occurs alone and the subject is not remaining for the second and third; and it indicates conjunction according to them both, so all occur at once and the subject accepts them. So he answered that in this example, only one divorce occurs according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because the implication of this speech is separation, so it does not change by 'wa'. And they both said its implication is conjunction, so it does not change by 'wa'. Meaning that this order according to him and conjunction according to them both did not come from 'wa', but from the implication of the speech. For the implication of the speech according to him is separation; if it were not so, he would have said: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced.' Since he did not say 'thrice' but rather said 'you are divorced and divorced and divorced', it is known that he intended separation, so each occurs separately; so the first occurs and there remains no subject for the second and third. According to them both, the implication of the speech is conjunction; because if it were not so, he would not have attached all three to one condition. So when he attached them as a whole, they occur all at once. And Fakh al-Islam and the author of 'al-Taqwim' inclined... for the non-consummated woman, he only said this because if the woman is consummated and it is said to her: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced divorced divorced', all three occur by agreement after the existence of the condition, because she is a subject for them. (al-Qamar) 'The first occurs': i.e. the first divorce occurs and she becomes separated by one, because she is non-consummated, and there is no waiting period for a non-consummated woman, so she does not remain a subject for the second and third. This is order; for if 'wa' did not indicate order according to him and it were for mere combination, all three divorces should occur at the existence of the condition. (al-Qamar) 'So it does not change' etc. for 'wa' is for mere combination, and it is realized in separation as well. (al-Qamar) 'So it does not change' etc. because 'wa' is for mere combination, and it is realized in conjunction as well. (al-Qamar) 'Did not come' for the Imam and his two companions agree that 'wa' is for mere combination. (al-Qamar) 'And he inclined' etc. Know first that order according to the Imam is established by the implication of the speech and its necessity, not by 'wa'. The necessity is that his statement: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' is a complete sentence that does not need what follows it. As for his statement 'and divorced and divorced', it is an incomplete sentence; it depends upon the first sentence necessarily, for the incomplete needs the complete in conveying meaning; if there were no conjunction, it would not convey meaning.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning the legal implication of the Arabic conjunction 'wa' (و). The issue is whether 'wa' inherently indicates order (tartib) or mere conjunction without order (muqarana). The commentator begins by citing two Quranic verses that are often used to argue that 'wa' implies order: the mention of Safa and Marwa in sequence, and the command 'Bow and prostrate'. He then presents the Hanafi response. For the first verse, he explains that the Prophet's understanding of order came from unrecited revelation (wahi ghayr matlu), not from the word 'wa' itself; the reference to the verse is merely to show emphasis through precedence in mention. For the second verse, he counters with another Quranic verse addressed to Maryam, 'Prostrate and bow', where order is not obligatory by consensus, proving that 'wa' does not necessarily imply sequence. The commentator then elaborates that grammarians like Sibawayh affirm that 'wa' can indicate either simultaneity or succession depending on context. The discussion moves to a practical fiqh example: a husband says to his non-consummated wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced'. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, only one divorce occurs because the wording implies separation (iftaq): each 'divorced' is separate, and after the first, the wife becomes completely separated (ba'in), leaving no subject for further divorces. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all three divorces occur simultaneously because the implication is conjunction (ijtima'), and the wife, being non-consummated, can still receive all three as she is a valid subject until divorced. The commentator clarifies that both positions derive not from the word 'wa' itself, but from the overall structure and necessity of the speech. He concludes by noting that all three imams agree that 'wa' is for mere combination (mujarrad al-jam'), and the differing results come from the implication of the particular phrasing. This passage is a classic example of how Hanafi usul relies on contextual factors rather than a fixed meaning of a term.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic conjunction 'and', which can indicate either order or mere combination depending on context, as per majority of grammarians.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order, sequence: the implication that the preceding element comes before the following.
المقارنة (al-muqarana): Conjunction, simultaneity: the joining of two items without inherent order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a man says to his non-consummated wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced', how many divorces occur upon entry?
A) One divorce, because the phrasing implies separation and the wife becomes completely separated after the first.
B) Three divorces, because 'wa' implies conjunction and all occur simultaneously.
C) Zero, because the condition is invalid.
D) The divorces are suspended until the wife's waiting period ends.

Key Takeaway
The conjunction 'wa' is neutral in Hanafi usul; its implication of order or combination is determined by the context and necessity of the speech, not by the word itself.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Conjunction Waw in Suspended Divorce: Order vs. Conjunction
Usul dispute on waw in talaq mu'allaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of mujib al-kalam to distinguish between order and conjunction in suspended divorce, and explain why Imam Abu Hanifa differs from the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The waw is neutral; the implication of the speech determines order or simultaneity in suspended divorce.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar explores a classic usul dispute about the conjunction waw. While all Hanafi masters agree on the linguistic meaning of waw (absolute conjunction), they differ on the 'implication of the speech' (mujib al-kalam) in a conditional divorce statement. This difference leads to opposite rulings on the number of divorces that occur when a non-virgin wife fulfills the condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is about the meaning of the waw in a suspended divorce statement like 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced.' Does the waw indicate order (sequential) or conjunction (simultaneous)?
2
State the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only one divorce occurs (order implies the first takes effect, then no capacity remains). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that three divorces occur (simultaneous).
Both agree the waw itself does not determine this; the difference lies in the overall implication of the speech.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof: If the speaker intended all three at once, he would have said 'thrice' (thalathan). By repeating 'divorced' with waw, he signals sequentiality. The Sahibayn's proof: Attaching all three to one condition shows they are intended to occur together; the condition applies equally to all.
Both arguments rely on the context of the speech, not just the literal meaning of waw.
4
Understand the role of mujib al-kalam
The term 'mujib al-kalam' refers to the necessary implication of the speech. For Abu Hanifa, the implication is separation (iftiraq) because the first sentence is complete, and the subsequent clauses are dependent. For the Sahibayn, the implication is conjunction (ijtima') because all three are linked to one condition.
This concept shows that the ruling is derived from the structure of the utterance, not from the waw particle alone.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: For a non-virgin wife (ghayr madkhul biha), if the condition is fulfilled, Abu Hanifa rules one divorce (she becomes separated and has no 'idda, so no capacity for further divorces), while the Sahibayn rule three divorces (all occur together because the condition applies to all).
The passage also notes later Hanafi scholars like Fakhr al-Islam and Ibn al-Humam prefer the Sahibayn's view.

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث وفي قوله لغير الموطوءة: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وطالق وطالق، جواب سؤال مقدر يرد علينا وهو أنه إذا قال أحد لامرأته الغير الموطوءة: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وطالق وطالق فعند أبي حنيفة لم تقع واحدة وعندهما: ثلاث فعلم أن الواو للترتيب عنده، فيقع الأول منفردًا ولم يبق المحل للثاني والثالث، وللمقارنة عندهما فيقع الكل دفعة واحدة، والمحل يقبلها، فأجاب بأن في هذا المثال إنما تطلق واحدة عند أبي حنيفة رحله؛ لأن موجب هذا الكلام الافتراق فلا يتغير بالواو، وقالا موجبه بين الطلقات الاجتماع، فلا يتغير بالواو يعني أن هذا الترتيب عنده والمقارنة عندهما لم يجئ من الواو، بل من موجب الكلام، فإن موجب الكلام عنده الافتراق؛ إذ لو لم يكن كذلك لقال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثلاثا، فإذا لم يقل: ثلاثًا بل قال: أنت طالق وطالق وطالق علم أنه قصد الافتراق، فيقع كلّ منها على حدة، فيقع الأول و لم يبق محل للثاني وللثالث، وعندهما: موجب الكلام الاجتماع؛ لأنه لو لم يكن كذلك لما علق الثلاث كله بشرط المرأة الغير المدخولة ما نافية واحد، فإذا علقه جملة وقع جملة واحدة، وقد مال فخر الإسلام وصاحب التقويم لغير الموطوءة إنما قال: هذا؛ لأن المرأة إذا كانت مدخولة، وقيل لها: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق طالق طالق، تقع الثلاثة بالاتفاق بعد وجود الشرط؛ لكونها محلاً لها. بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث ٣٢٧ بحث الواو إلى رجحان قولهما في وقوع الثلاث، وهذا كله إذا قدم الشرط، وإن أخره بأن قال: أنت طالق وطالق وطالق إن دخلت الدار يقع الثلاث اتفاقا؛ لأنه وجد في آخر الكلام ما يغير أوله وهو الشرط، فتوقف الأول على آخره فيقعن جملةً. وإذا قال لغير الموطوءة: أنت طالق وطالق وطالق، إنما تبين بواحدة، جواب سؤال آخر على علمائنا له وهو: أن يقال: إذ أنجز الطلاق بدون الشرط لغير الموطوءة بأن يقول: أنت طالق وطالق وطالق فعلماؤنا الثلاثة لله اتفقوا على أنه تقع الواحدة ههنا، ففهم أنه للترتيب عند الكل، فأجاب بأن في هذه المسألة إنما تبين بواحدة؛ لأن الناقصة شيئًا، فإذا عطفت على قوله: فأنت طالق تعلقت بالشرط وهو قوله: إن دخلت الدار بواسطة، فكان الأول متعلقا بالشرط بغير واسطة، والثاني بواسطة والثالث بواسطتين بالترتيب، وإذا وجد الشرط ينزلن بالترتيب السابق بأن تقع الأولى أولاً ثم الثانية، فإذا وقعت الأولى لم يبق المحل للثانية والثالثة؛ لكونها غير مدخولة بها، فتبين بواحدة وأما الصاحبان فقالا: إن موجب الكلام الاجتماع والاشتراك في الشرط، فساوت الثانية والثالثة الأولى في التحقيق بالشرط بلا واسطة وصار كأنه كرر الشرط بأن قال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وإن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وإن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق، فإذا وجد الشرط وقعن جملة واحدة، ثم اعلم أنه لا ينتقض أصل الإمام بآية الوضوء؛ لأن الترتيب ثمه في الإيجاب لا في الواجب كما في قوله : إذا جاء غد فاشتر لي غلامًا وجارية واستأجر دابةً، أما ههنا فإيقاع مرتب معلق فينزل، واختار فخر الإسلام وصاحب التقويم قول الصاحبين لعله لما قال في حاشية قمر الأقمار فأنظره ،ثمه ولم أجد وجه اختيارهما في ما عندي من كتب الأصول، لكن الإمام ابن الهمام قال في شرحه للهداية: وقولهما أرجح، ويفهم وجهه كلامه هناك. Statement of the sections of the third division. And in his statement to the non-virgin: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced' is an answer to an implied objection that comes to us, namely that if someone says to his non-virgin wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced,' then according to Abu Hanifa not one divorce occurs, and according to them two divorces occur three? So it is known that the waw indicates order according to him, so the first occurs alone and the place remains not for the second and third; and it indicates simultaneity according to them, so all occur at once, and the place accepts them. He answered that in this example only one divorce occurs according to Abu Hanifa because the implication of this speech is separation, so it does not change by the waw. And they said its implication between the divorces is conjunction, so it does not change by the waw. That is, this order according to him and simultaneity according to them did not come from the waw, but from the implication of the speech. For the implication of the speech according to him is separation; because if it were not so, he would have said: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced thrice.' If he delays it by saying: 'You are divorced and divorced and divorced if you enter the house,' then three occur by agreement, because what changes the first is found at the end of the speech, which is the condition, so the first is suspended on the last, so they occur as a whole. And if he says to a non-virgin: 'You are divorced and divorced and divorced,' she is only separated by one? Answer to another objection to our scholars: It is said: When he executes the divorce without condition for a non-virgin by saying: 'You are divorced and divorced and divorced,' then our three scholars agreed that one occurs here, so it is understood that order is according to all. He answered that in this case she is only separated by one because the incomplete sentence, when attached to his statement 'you are divorced' becomes connected to the condition via an intermediary. So the first is connected to the condition without an intermediary, the second with one intermediary, and the third with two intermediaries, in order. When the condition is found, they descend in the previous order: the first occurs, then the second. When the first occurs, there remains no place for the second and third because she is a non-virgin? Actually non-virgin means not previously touched? The text says 'ghayr madkhul biha' meaning she has not been entered? So she is a virgin? Actually 'ghayr madkhul biha' means she has not been touched (virgin) and there is no 'idda for her. So she is separated by one. And the two companions said the implication of the speech is conjunction and sharing in the condition, so the second and third become equal to the first in being truly connected to the condition without any intermediary, and it becomes as if he repeated the condition: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced; and if you enter the house, you are divorced; and if you enter the house, you are divorced.' So when the condition is found, they all occur at once. Then know that the principle of the Imam is not refuted by the verse of wudu, because the order there is in obligation not in the obligated, as in his statement: 'If tomorrow comes, buy for me a slave and a slave girl and hire an animal.' But here it is a suspended ordered occurrence, so it descends. And Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Taqwim chose the statement of the two companions. Perhaps because it was said in the margin of Qamar al-Aqmar? 'Unthirhu thumma'? I have not found the reason for their choice in the books of usul that I have. But Imam Ibn al-Humam said in his commentary on al-Hidayah: 'Their statement is more preponderant, and the reason for it is understood from his discussion there.' (al-Sanbali) to the preponderance of their statement. And an objection is raised to the Imam's statement: the suspended [divorce] is not actual divorce in the present, but rather it has the potential to become divorce upon existence of the condition. As long as it is not divorce in the present, it does not accept the description of order, because the attribute does not precede the subject. So the consideration is at the time of occurrence, and there is found in it nothing that necessitates different times of occurrence. Thus said Ibn al-Malik. (al-Qamar) 'So the first is suspended...' that the first part of the speech is suspended on the last if there is something in the last that changes it, and here the condition is a changer. So when the condition is uttered, the three become suspended, so they occur all together when the condition is found. (al-Qamar) For the non-virgin he said this because if the woman is a virgin? Actually 'mawtu'a' means touched. If she is a virgin? The text says 'mawtu'a' meaning touched? Actually 'mawtu'a' is passive participle meaning 'touched' (i.e., non-virgin). So if she is a non-virgin? The text says 'if the woman is a non-virgin, the three occur with this wording because the place remains due to the existence of the 'idda after divorce.' (al-Qamar) 'When he executes' i.e., he actually effects it without suspension on a condition. (al-Qamar) Also, 'from'? 'who occurs at'? Incomplete.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage examines a key usul dispute regarding the conjunction waw (و) in the context of suspended divorce (talaq mu'allaq). The ruling: If a man says to his non-virgin (ghayr madkhul biha) wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced,' Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only one divorce occurs, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that three divorces occur. This difference is not due to the waw itself—all three agree that waw is for absolute conjunction (mutlaq al-jam'). Rather, the disagreement stems from the 'implication of the speech' (mujib al-kalam). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the natural implication is separation (iftiraq) because if the speaker intended all three at once, he would have said 'thrice' (thalathan). By repeating 'divorced' with waw, he signals sequential occurrence. Thus, the first divorce takes effect upon the condition, and since the wife is non-virgin (no 'idda), there is no remaining capacity for subsequent divorces. On the other hand, the Sahibayn argue that the implication is conjunction (ijtima'), because the speaker attached all three to a single condition, showing he intended them all to occur together. The passage then addresses variations: if the condition is delayed (e.g., 'You are divorced and divorced and divorced if you enter the house'), there is consensus on three divorces because the condition at the end changes the meaning of the beginning. If the divorces are executed directly (munajjiz) without a condition, all three agree that only one divorce occurs, confirming that the waw does not indicate order inherently. The passage also includes later Hanafi opinions: Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Taqwim side with the Sahibayn, and Ibn al-Humam considers their view stronger. The objection that the suspended divorce is not actual divorce until the condition occurs is addressed: the attribute of order cannot precede the subject, so at the moment of occurrence, there is no basis for sequential timing. Finally, the example of wudu verse is distinguished: order there is in obligation, not in the obligated act, unlike here where the occurrence itself is ordered.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic conjunction 'and', which can indicate either order (tartib) or mere conjunction (jam') depending on context and the implication of the speech.
موجب الكلام (mujib al-kalam): The necessary implication or requirement of the speech itself, distinguished from the literal meaning of individual words like the waw.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Sequential order; in this context, the divorces occur one after another.
الاجتماع (al-ijtima'): Simultaneity; all items occur together at once.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example where a man says to his non-virgin wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and divorced and divorced,' what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Three divorces occur
B) One divorce occurs
C) Two divorces occur
D) No divorce occurs

Key Takeaway
The waw does not inherently indicate order or conjunction; the implication of the entire speech (mujib al-kalam) determines the ruling in suspended divorce.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Waw Dispute: Conjunction vs. Circumstance in 'Tallaqni wa laka alfu'
Analyzing the waw types and the dispute over a wife's statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding the default meaning of waw to derive the legal consequence in a disputed scenario.

Core Idea
The waw's default is conjunction; only a clear contextual shift to a circumstantial meaning can alter the ruling.

This passage delves into a classic usul dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn over the interpretation of waw in a wife's statement. The disagreement hinges on whether the waw is conjunctive (عطف) or circumstantial (حال), leading to different rulings on whether compensation is due in a divorce. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify when a text's literal meaning can be overridden by contextual clues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed text and the two interpretations
Read the wife's statement 'Tallaqni wa laka alfu dirham' and note that the waw can be interpreted as either conjunctive (just adding a statement) or circumstantial (setting a condition).
The two interpretations lead to opposite rulings on compensation.
2
Analyze the Hanafi principle on the default waw
Apply the usul rule: al-asl fi al-waw al-atf (the original meaning of waw is conjunction). This means that unless there is strong contextual evidence, the waw simply conjoins two independent clauses.
Abu Hanifa adheres to this default.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's argument for a circumstantial reading
Consider their reasoning: the context of khul' (wife-initiated divorce with compensation) suggests that the waw introduces a circumstance (hal), making the second clause a condition for the first.
They analogize to the Quranic example of 'khalideen' as an estimated circumstance.
4
Review the Quranic evidence (hal muqaddara) used by both sides
Both sides invoke the verse 'fadkhuluha khalideen' where 'khalideen' is a circumstantial accusative estimated at the time of entry. The Hanafi side uses it to show that a circumstance can be estimated (muqaddara), while the Sahibayn use it to argue that the waw can introduce such an estimated circumstance.
The difference lies in whether the waw itself is considered circumstantial or just the noun.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) in the divorce ruling
If the waw is conjunctive (Abu Hanifa): divorce occurs without compensation, and the wife owes nothing. If the waw is circumstantial (Sahibayn): the divorce becomes a khul', requiring the wife to pay the thousand and is irrevocable (ba'in).
The practical consequence is a significant financial and marital distinction.

بحث الواو
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث أي كن حرًا وأنت مؤد للألف، وبأنه من قبيل الحال المقدرة أي أد إلى ألفا حال كونك مقدرا أن الحرية في حال الأداء، فتكون الحرية موقوفة عليه، وبأن الجملة الحالية قائمة مقام جواب الأمر كأنه قيل: "أد" إلى ألفًا" فتصر حرًا، وبأن الحرية حال الأداء، والحال وصف في المعنى، والوصف لا يتقدم على الموصوف فالحرية لا تتقدم على الأداء. وقد تكون لعطف الجملة، هذا يصلح أن تكون على الحقيقة، وإنما أخرها عن بيان الحال التي هي مجاز ليتفرع عليه المثال المختلف فيه على ما سيأتي، ويحتمل أن تكون للمجاز؛ لأن أصل العطف هو المشاركة في الحكم لم يوجد ههنا، وإنما هي في مجرد الثبوت والوقوع

المشاركة من قبيل الحال المقدرة: فإن غرض المتكلم من هذا الكلام عدم وقوع الحرية في الحال كما في قوله تعالى: فَادْخُلُوهَا خَالِدِينَ (الزمر :۷۳) أي مقدرين الخلود حال الدخول. (القمر) الحال المقدرة إلخ أي المفروضة، فمعنى المثال المذكور في المتن: أن أد إلى ألفًا حال كونك مقدرًا أي فارضا أن الحرية في حال الأداء وإن كان الواقع خلاف ذلك؛ لأن الأداء قبل الحرية، والحرية بعده.(السنبلي) قائمة: لكونها مقصودة المتكلم. قائمة مقام جواب الأمر إلخ كان يرد عليه أن جواب الأمر لا يكون إلا فعلاً مضارعا والجملة الحالية ههنا جملة اسمية فكيف يصح كونها جوابًا للأمر، فقال الشارح مجيبا لذلك كأنه قيل: أد إلى ألفا إلخ فافهم (السنبلي كأنه قيل :إلخ فكانت الحرية متعلقة بالأداء وموقوفة عليه، فإن المعنى إن أديت إلى ألفا فتصر حرا، واعترض عليه ابن الملك بأن كونها قائمة مقام جواب الأمر مجرد اصطلاح، فلا يلتفت إليه، فلو كان معنى الكلام أدّ إلى ألفًا تصر حرًا لم يبق واو الحال وكلامنا فيه. (القمر) حال الأداء فيه أن الحرية حال المؤدي لا حال الأداء تأمل. (القمر) لا تتقدم على الأداء: فلا يعتق إلا بالأداء. (القمر) هذا أي كون الواو لعطف الجملة. (القمر) وإنما أخرها أي الواو التي لعطف الجملة. (القمر) وإنما أخرها إلخ هذا دفع توهم تقريره: أن قول المصنف لعطف الجملة لما أمكن أن يكون بيانًا لمعنى الواو ،حقيقة، فلزم على هذا التقدير في عبارة المصنف وقوع معنى مجازي للواو بين معنييه الحقيقيين، فاختل الكلام بذلك، فدفعه بقوله : وإنما أخرها، وتقريره ظاهر. (السنبلي) ليتفرع إلخ: وفيه إشارة إلى رد ما قال أعظم العلماء أي مولانا عبد السلام أعظمي له من أن كون الواو لعطف الجملة ليس حقيقة الواو وإلا فذكره بعد الحال مشكل (القمر) المثال المختلف فيه أي ما إذا قالت امرأة طلقني ولك ألف درهم (القمر) المشاركة أي بين المعطوف والمعطوف عليه . (القمر) ههنا : أي في عطف الجملة على الجملة. (القمر) مجرد الثبوت والوقوع لأن الجملتين لا تشارك بينهما في الحكم. (المحشي)

فلا تجب به المشاركة في الخبر كقوله : "هذه طالق ثلاثًا وهذه طالق" فتطلق الثانية واحدة فقط؛ لأن كلا من الجملتين تامة لا يفتقر إحداهما إلى الأخرى، والعطف ليس إلا لمجرد سياقة الكلام. وكذا في قولها طلقني ولك ألف درهم حتى إذا طلقها لا يجب شيء للزوج عليها عند أبي حنيفة محله؛ لأن قولها: "ولك" ألف" معطوف على ما سبق، وليس للحال حتى يكون أي قوله: "طلقني" شرطًا ؛ لأن أصل الطلاق أن يكون بلا مال؛ لأنه إن ذكر المال سمي خلعا ، ويصير يمينا من جانبه، وليس أيضًا من صيغ الوعد والنذر حتى يلزم عليها وفاؤه، فكان لغوا وفيه تأمل. وقالا إنها للحال فيصير شرطا وبدلاً، فيجب الألف يعني أن عندهما هذه الواو ليست للعطف كما كانت عنده بل للحال والحال في معنى الشرط للعامل، فيصير كأنها قالت: "طلقني"، والحال أن لك ألفًا علي، فلمّا قال: "طلقتُ" كان تقديره طلقتُ بذلك الشرط، فكان معاوضة في معنى الخلع، فيجب الألف ويكون الطلاق بائنا.

الزوج على الزوجة
المشاركة أي بين الجملة المعطوفة والجملة المعطوفة عليها. (القمر) فتطلق الثانية إلخ إذ ليس ذكر العدد في الجملة الثانية ولو كان غرض المتكلم المشاركة في الخبر لقال: هذه طالق ثلاثًا وهذه، فيكون عطف المفرد، ويلزم الشركة في الخبر. (القمر) يمينًا من جانبه أي من جانب الزوج؛ لأن الزوج يصير معلقا للطلاق على قبولها المال والتعليق بالشرط يمين. (القمر) وليس أي قوله: "ولك ألف درهم . (القمر) صيغ الوعد إلخ: صيغة الوعد بأن تقول مثلاً طلقني أودي لك ألف درهم وصيغة النذر بأن تقول مثلاً طلقني وعلي لك ألف درهم المحشي) وفيه تأمل لعله إشارة إلى أن هذا الكلام وعدة ألف ألبتة، فيجب الألف بالوعدة وليس عوضا عن الطلاق، قال الحموي في شرح "الأشباه " : قال السبكي ظاهر الآيات والسنة تقتضي وجوب الوفاء انتهى وفي "الأشباه" الخلف في الوعد حرام كذا في أضحية "الذخيرة" انتهى. (القمر) فكان معاوضة إلخ فإن سؤال الطلاق من المرأة يكون بطريق المعاوضة في غالب الأمر، فقولها: "طلقني" يكون بمعنى خالعني، فكأنها قالت: "خالعني ولك ألف درهم والجواب من الإمام أن أصل الطلاق أن يكون بلا مال، والمعاوضة فيه من العوارض وأصل الواو العطف، فلا يترك ما هو الأصل برعاية العوارض، فإن ترك القوي برعاية الضعيف باطل . (القمر) ويكون الطلاق بائنا كما هو حكم الخلع على ما مر . (القمر)
Discussion of the waw. Explanation of the types of the third division: It is as if he said, 'Be free and you are paying the thousand.' And it is of the type of the estimated circumstance, meaning: pay a thousand while you are estimating that freedom is at the time of payment, so freedom is dependent upon it. And the circumstantial sentence stands in the place of the command's answer, as if it was said: 'Pay a thousand' so you become free. And because freedom is at the time of payment, and the circumstance is a description in meaning, and the description cannot precede the described, so freedom cannot precede the payment. And it may be for conjunction of sentences. This could be literal, and he only delayed it after explaining the circumstance which is metaphorical, so that the disputed example can branch from it as will come. And it is possible it is metaphorical, because the essence of conjunction is sharing in the ruling, which does not exist here, but rather it is merely in [the fact of] existence and occurrence. The sharing is of the type of estimated circumstance: for the speaker's intention from this speech is the non-occurrence of freedom at the present moment, as in His statement, the Exalted: 'So enter it, eternally [residing]' (Az-Zumar:73), meaning estimating eternity at the time of entry. (Al-Qamar) 'Estimated circumstance' etc., i.e., assumed. So the meaning of the example mentioned in the text is: that you pay a thousand while you are estimating, i.e., assuming, that freedom is at the time of payment, even if the reality is contrary to that, because payment is before freedom, and freedom is after it. (As-Sunbuli) 'Stands': because it is intended by the speaker. 'Stands in the place of the command's answer' etc. An objection could be raised that the answer to command can only be a present tense verb, but the circumstantial sentence here is a nominal sentence, so how can it be an answer to the command? The commentator replied to that: 'As if it was said: pay a thousand' etc., so understand. (As-Sunbuli) 'As if it was said' etc., so freedom becomes linked to payment and dependent upon it, for the meaning is: if you pay a thousand, you become free. Ibn al-Malik objected that its standing in the place of the command's answer is merely a convention, so it should not be considered. If the meaning of the speech were 'pay a thousand, you become free', there would be no waw of circumstance, and our discussion is about it. (Al-Qamar) 'At the time of payment' here means that freedom is at the time of the payer, not at the time of payment. Consider. (Al-Qamar) 'It cannot precede payment': so he is not freed except with payment. (Al-Qamar) 'This' i.e., that the waw is for conjunction of sentences. (Al-Qamar) 'And he only delayed it' i.e., the waw that is for conjunction of sentences. (Al-Qamar) 'And he only delayed it' etc. This is a refutation of a misunderstanding. Its explanation: that the author's statement 'for conjunction of sentences' could be an explanation of the literal meaning of the waw. So based on this assumption, in the author's expression, a metaphorical meaning of the waw would occur between its two literal meanings, thus the speech becomes disordered. So he refuted it with his statement 'and he only delayed it', and its explanation is apparent. (As-Sunbuli) 'So that the disputed example can branch' etc.: In it is a reference to refuting what the greatest scholar, i.e., our master Abdul Salam Azmi, said: that the waw being for conjunction of sentences is not the literal meaning of the waw, otherwise mentioning it after the circumstance would be problematic (Al-Qamar) The disputed example, i.e., when a woman says: 'Divorce me and you have a thousand dirhams.' (Al-Qamar) 'Sharing' i.e., between the coordinate part and the base part. (Al-Qamar) 'Here' i.e., in conjunction of a sentence with a sentence. (Al-Qamar) 'Merely existence and occurrence' because the two sentences do not share in the ruling. (Al-Mahshi) So sharing in the predicate is not necessitated by it, as in his statement: 'This one is thrice divorced and this one is divorced' so the second is divorced only once; because each of the two sentences is complete, neither needs the other, and the conjunction is only for mere flow of speech. Similarly, in her statement 'Divorce me and you have a thousand dirhams', even if he divorces her, nothing is due to the husband from her according to Abu Hanifa, his locus; because her statement 'and you have a thousand' is conjoined to what preceded, and not for circumstance such that his statement 'divorce me' would be a condition; because the original in divorce is without compensation; because if compensation is mentioned, it is called khul', and it becomes an oath from his side, and it is also not from the formula of promise or vow such that she would be obliged to fulfill it. So it is null, and in it there is consideration. And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is for circumstance, so it becomes a condition and a substitute, so the thousand is obligatory. That is: according to them, this waw is not for conjunction as it was with him, but for circumstance, and the circumstance is in the meaning of a condition for the agent, so it becomes as if she said: 'Divorce me' while the circumstance is that you have a thousand upon me. So when he said 'I divorced', the estimation was 'I divorced by that condition', so it was a compensation in the meaning of khul', so the thousand is obligatory, and the divorce becomes irrevocable. The husband upon the wife. 'Sharing' i.e., between the conjoined sentence and the sentence it is conjoined to. (Al-Qamar) 'So the second is divorced' etc. Since the number is not mentioned in the second sentence. If the speaker's intention were sharing in the predicate, he would say: 'This one is thrice divorced and this one', making it conjunction of a single word, necessitating sharing in the predicate. (Al-Qamar) 'An oath from his side' i.e., from the husband's side, because the husband becomes a suspender of divorce upon her acceptance of the compensation, and suspension by condition is an oath. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is not' i.e., his statement 'and you have a thousand dirhams' (Al-Qamar) 'formulas of promise' etc.: A formula of promise is like saying, for example: 'Divorce me and I will pay you a thousand dirhams.' And a formula of vow is like saying, for example: 'Divorce me and upon me is a thousand dirhams for you.' (Al-Mahshi) 'And in it there is consideration' perhaps an indication that this speech is a promise of a thousand absolutely, so the thousand is obligatory by the promise and not compensation for divorce. Al-Hamawi in his commentary on al-Ashbah said: As-Subki said: The apparent meanings of Quranic verses and Sunnah necessitate the obligation of fulfilling promises. End. And in al-Ashbah: breaking a promise is forbidden. Likewise in the sacrifice of adh-Dhakhira. End. (Al-Qamar) 'So it was a compensation' etc. Because the wife's request for divorce is by way of compensation in most cases. So her statement 'divorce me' is in the meaning of 'make khul' with me', as if she said: 'make khul' with me and you have a thousand dirhams.' And the response from the Imam is that the original in divorce is without compensation, and compensation in it is an accidental matter, and the original rule of the waw is conjunction, so the original should not be abandoned in observance of accidental matters, because abandoning the strong in observance of the weak is invalid. (Al-Qamar) 'And the divorce becomes irrevocable' just as is the ruling of khul' as has passed. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the different types of the letter waw (و), focusing on the third division as a conjunction of sentences (عطف الجملة) versus a circumstantial waw (واو الحال). The commentator explains that when someone says, 'Be free and you are paying a thousand,' the waw can be interpreted as an estimated circumstance (حال مقدرة), meaning the freedom is contingent upon payment. This is supported by the Quranic example 'Enter it, eternally [residing]' where the eternity is estimated at the time of entry. The discussion then moves to a disputed example: a wife says to her husband, 'Divorce me and you have a thousand dirhams.' According to Abu Hanifa, the waw here is for conjunction (عطف), so the statement 'you have a thousand' is simply added to the request without making it a condition. Therefore, if the husband divorces her, he is not entitled to the money because the original basis of divorce is without compensation. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the waw is for circumstance (حال), making the second clause a condition, so the divorce becomes a khul' (divorce for compensation), obligating the wife to pay the thousand and making the divorce irrevocable (بائن). The commentator also addresses objections and supports Abu Hanifa's position by noting that the original rule of waw is conjunction and the original in divorce is without compensation; abandoning these principles for accidental considerations is invalid.

Key Terms
واو الحال (waw al-hal): The waw that introduces a circumstantial clause (حال), indicating the state of the subject at the time of the action.
واو العطف (waw al-atf): The waw that conjoins two sentences, implying mere sequence or addition without implying a conditional relationship.
حال مقدرة (hal muqaddara): An estimated circumstance; a state that is assumed to exist at the time of the action even if it does not actually occur until later.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa (رحمه الله), if a wife says to her husband 'Tallaqni wa laka alfu dirham' (Divorce me and you have a thousand dirhams) and the husband divorces her, what is the ruling?
A) The wife must pay the thousand dirhams and the divorce is irrevocable (ba'in).
B) The wife owes nothing and the divorce is valid without compensation.
C) The husband must pay the wife a thousand dirhams.
D) The divorce is invalid because it is conditional.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of waw in conditional statements can change the entire ruling; the Hanafi usul preserves the original meaning unless a clear contextual shift is proven.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

The Particle Thumma: Delay in Utterance or Judgment?
Dispute on the linguistic meaning of 'thumma' and its application to conditional divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the particle 'thumma' and identify its practical consequences in conditional divorces.

Core Idea
Thumma implies delay; but is it in speech or ruling? The answer changes divorce outcomes.

The simple Arabic particle 'thumma' (then) seems straightforward, but its precise legal meaning has been a point of contention among Hanafi jurists. This lesson unpacks the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether 'thumma' indicates a delay in the utterance itself or only in the legal judgment. The resolution of this linguistic nuance has direct consequences for the validity of conditional divorces and other declarations.

Guided Path
1
State the positions
Identify Abu Hanifa's view: delay in both utterance and judgment. Identify the Sahibayn's view: delay only in judgment, acting on the apparent connectedness of the wording.
The source text calls Abu Hanifa's view 'the complete form' (al-kamil).
2
Analyze the proofs
Examine the linguistic evidence. Abu Hanifa argues that in declarations (insha'at), a delayed judgment with a connected utterance is impossible. The Sahibayn rely on the literal, connected wording (zahir).
The commentator notes that Abu Hanifa's proof is specific to declarations, not reports (akhbar).
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence lies in conditional divorces. Study the four scenarios involving a non-consummated or consummated wife with a presented or delayed condition.
The source text details four outcomes. Focus on how the differing views on 'thumma' produce different rulings.
4
Apply to the scenarios
Work through the example: to a non-consummated wife, he says 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house'. Apply both views and note the results.
Under Abu Hanifa, only the first divorce occurs; the rest are void. Under the Sahibayn, the results differ.
5
Evaluate the dispute
Consider the methodological difference: Abu Hanifa's holistic view vs. the Sahibayn's adherence to the apparent wording. Reflect on how this affects legal reasoning in usul al-fiqh.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are respected.

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث
بحث "ثم"
و "ثم" للتراخي بمنزلة ما لو سكت ثم استأنف فإذا قال: "أنت طالق ثم طالق" فكأنه سكت على قوله: "أنت طالق" وبعد ذلك قال: "ثم طالق" وهذا هو الكامل في التراخي أي في التكلم والحكم جميعًا، وهو مذهب أبي حنيفة ؛ لأن التراخي في الحكم مع الوصل في التكلم ممتنع في الإنشاءات، فلما كان الحكم متراخيا كان التكلم متراخيا تقديرا، وعندهما التراخي في الحكم مع الوصل في التكلم عملا بالظاهر ؛ لأن ظاهر اللفظ موصول مع الأول، والعطف لا يصح مع الانفصال، فكان الأولى هو التراخي في الحكم فقط، وثمرة هذا الخلاف ما بينه بقوله: حتى إذا قال لغير المدخول بها: أنت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق إن دخلت الدار فعنده يقع الأول ويلغو ما بعده؛ لأن التراخي لما كان في التكلم فكأنه للتراخي: أي تراخي وجود المعطوف عن المعطوف عليه، فإذا قلت: "جاءني زيد ثم عمرو" وكان المعنى أنه وقع بينهما مهلة (القمر) وهذا هو الكامل إلخ فيه إيماء إلى دليل الإمام الأعظم تقريره : أن "ثم" موضوعة لمطلق التراخي، والمطلق ينصرف إلى الفرد الكامل والكامل في التراخي هو التراخي في التكلم والحكم جميعًا، ولو كان التراخي في الحكم دون التكلم كما قال صاحباه لكان ثابتا من وجه دون وجه وفيه أن هذا النحو من الكمال أي جعل الوصل الموجود الثابت في التكلم هدرًا لا يساعده العرف من أهل العرب واللغة في كلمة "ثم" تأمل. (القمر) ممتنع إلخ : فإن الأحكام لا تتراخى عن التكلم في الإنشاءات، فلما كان إلخ ثم لا يخفى ما فيه، فإن هذا الدليل بالإنشاءات، فلا يثبت كون "ثم" للتراخي في التكلم والحكم جميعا في الأخبار تأمل. (القمر) حتى إذا قال إلخ قلت بيان الاختلاف بين أبي حنيفة لله وصاحبيه في هذه المسألة وهي أربعة أوجه؛ لأنه إما إن علق الطلاق بكلمة "ثم" في غير المدخول بها أو في المدخول بها وفي كل واحد إما إن أخر الشرط أو قدمه، ففي الأولى أي في غير المدخول بها بتقديم الشرط عنده يتعلق الأولى بدخول الدار، وتقع الثانية في الحال، ولغت الثالثة، وفي الثاني أي في غير المدخول بها بتأخير الشرط وقعت الأولى في الحال ولغت الثانية والثالثة، وفي الثالثة أي في المدخول بها بتقديم الشرط تعلقت الأولى بدخول الدار، وتقع ثنتان في الحال، وفي الرابعة أي في المدخول بها بتأخير الشرط وقعت ثنتان في الحال وتعلقت الثالثة بدخول الدار. (السنبلي)
Statement of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of 'thumma'. And 'thumma' is for delay (tarakhi), analogous to if one is silent then resumes. So if he says: 'You are divorced, then divorced', it is as if he paused after saying 'You are divorced' and after that said: 'then divorced'. This is the complete form of delay, i.e., in both the utterance and the judgment, and this is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. Because delay in judgment while the utterance is connected is impossible in declarations (insha'at). So when the judgment is delayed, the utterance is also delayed by implication. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the delay is in the judgment while the utterance is connected, acting upon the apparent (zahir), because the apparent meaning of the wording is connected to the first, and conjunction is not valid with separation. So the better view is delay in judgment only. The fruit of this disagreement is what he clarifies by saying: Until when he says to a non-consummated wife: 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house', then according to him (Abu Hanifa) the first occurs and what follows is void; because the delay being in the utterance, it is as if he said... (al-Qamar) 'And this is the complete' etc. contains an indication of the proof of the Greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa). Its explanation: that 'thumma' is placed for absolute delay, and the absolute is directed toward the complete individual, and the complete in delay is delay in both utterance and judgment. If the delay were in judgment without utterance as his two companions said, it would be established from one aspect not another. And in this, that this kind of completeness, i.e., making the existing connection in utterance null and void, is not supported by the custom of the Arabs and language of the word 'thumma'. Ponder. (al-Qamar) 'Impossible' etc.: because judgments cannot be delayed from the utterance in declarations. So when it was... then it is not hidden what is in it, for this proof is specific to declarations, so it does not establish that 'thumma' is for delay in both utterance and judgment in reports (akhbar). Ponder. (al-Qamar) 'Until when he says' etc. I said: Explanation of the difference between Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) and his two companions in this issue, and it has four aspects: because either he suspends divorce with the word 'thumma' in a non-consummated wife or in a consummated one, and in each case either he delays the condition or presents it. So in the first, i.e., in non-consummated with presenting the condition, according to him the first is suspended on entering the house, the second occurs immediately, and the third is void. In the second, i.e., in non-consummated with delaying the condition, the first occurs immediately, and the second and third are void. In the third, i.e., in consummated with presenting the condition, the first is suspended on entering the house, and two occur immediately. In the fourth, i.e., in consummated with delaying the condition, two occur immediately and the third is suspended on entering the house. (al-Sinbali)
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage discusses the particle 'thumma' (then) and its implication of delay (tarakhi). The core issue is whether 'thumma' indicates delay in both the utterance (speaking) and the judgment (legal effect) or only in the judgment. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that because in declarations (insha'at) the judgment cannot be delayed while the utterance is connected, the delay must be in both; therefore, when a man says 'You are divorced, then divorced', it is as if he paused between the two utterances. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the apparent wording is connected, so delay is only in the judgment; the utterance is considered continuous. The practical consequence (thamarah) is in a conditional divorce: for a non-consummated wife, if he says 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house', Abu Hanifa rules that only the first divorce occurs, and the subsequent ones are void because the delay in utterance breaks the sequence. The Sahibayn would have different rulings. The text then elaborates the four scenarios depending on the status of the wife (consummated or not) and whether the condition is presented or delayed. This dispute illustrates how a subtle linguistic analysis of a particle can have significant effects on fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle indicating delay (tarakhi). Abu Hanifa: delay in both utterance and judgment. Sahibayn: delay only in judgment.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): Delay or postponement; the meaning of 'thumma'.
الإنشاءات (al-insha'at): Declarative utterances that create a legal effect, such as divorce, sale, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a man says to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced, then divorced, then divorced if you enter the house', what is the ruling?
A) All three divorces occur immediately
B) The first divorce occurs, the rest are void
C) The first and second occur immediately, the third is conditional
D) All three are conditional on entering the house

Key Takeaway
The particle 'thumma' in Hanafi usul generates an intra-madhab dispute on whether delay is in utterance or judgment, with direct impact on the validity of sequential divorces.
